وأما تعلقهم بأنه لم يحضر بدراً فإنه جهل عظيم؛ لأن أكثر ما في أن يكون غيره أفضل منه وقد بينا أن إمامة المفضول جائزة مع حصول الفاضل بسبب عارض يقعده على أن الفضيلة له في تأخره عن بدر ثابتة لأنه إنما تأخر بأمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم له بذلك وإلزامه له لتعليل ابنته ومشاهدة أمرها لأن بنت الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم قد كانت مرضت فأمره بالقيام عليها وكان صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: إن قوماً بالمدينة تخلفوا وما تخلفوا عما نحن فيه، قال الراوي: فكنا نرى أنه يعني عثمان وقد جعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم له فضل الحاضرين وضرب له سهمه من غنيمة بدر ولو علم أنه مؤثر للتخلف عن الغزو لغير عذر لكان حرياً بذمه والتنبيه على فعله ورأيه فيه وهذا عائد بالطعن على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والتهمة سوء له دون غيره. وأما تعلقهم بتأخره عن بيعة الرضوان فإنه غفلة وجهل ولجاج وعناد وذلك أنه إنما تأخر لتحمل رسالة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى أهل مكة حتى قتل علي [؟] وقال الزبير استعمله علي على المدينة ثم إن قثم سار أيام معاوية إلى سمرقند مع سعيد بن عثمان بن عفان فمات بها شهيداً وكان يشبه النبي وروي أن ابن عباس نعى إليه أخوه قثم وهو في منزله فاسترجع وأناخ عن الطريق فصلى ركعتين فأطال فيهما الجلوس ثم قام إلى راحلته وهو يقرأ واستعينوا بالصبر والصلاة وإنها لكبيرة إلا على الخاشعين ولم يعقب قثم. حين أرجف بالعسكر أن قريشاً قتلت عثمان فغضب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقلق وقال: والله لئن كان قتلوه لأضرمنها عليهم ناراً؛ ثم أخذ لأجل هذا الخبر على الصحابة بيعة الرضوان وقال: هذه شمالي عن يمين عثمان وهي خير له من يمينه؛ فهو كان سبب بيعة الرضوان وغضب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فكيف يكون بتأخره عنها منقوصا؟ فدل جميع ما وصفناه على فضل عثمان ونزاهته وعدالته وسلامة بيعته وأنه قتل مظلوماً.
As for their attachment (objection) that he did not attend Badr, it is great ignorance; because at most it would mean that someone else is better than him, and we have shown that the imamate of the less excellent is permissible when the more excellent is present due to an incidental hindrance, and moreover the virtue for him in his delay from Badr is established because he only delayed by the command of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for that and his imposition upon him to attend to his daughter and oversee her affair, because the daughter of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had fallen ill, so he ordered him to care for her, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to say: 'Indeed there are people in Medina who fell behind and they did not fall behind from what we are in.' The narrator said: 'We used to think that he meant Uthman, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had given him the merit of those present and allotted him his share of the booty of Badr, and if he had known that he preferred to stay behind from the expedition without excuse, he would have been deserving of blame and censure for his action and opinion in it, and this would have been an attack on the Prophet (peace be upon him) and an evil accusation against him and not others.' As for their attachment (objection) regarding his delay from the Pledge of Ridwan, it is carelessness, ignorance, obstinacy, and stubbornness, because he only delayed to carry the message of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to the people of Mecca until Ali [?] was killed, and al-Zubayr said: 'Ali appointed him over Medina.' Then Qutham went during the days of Muawiya to Samarkand with Said ibn Uthman ibn Affan and died there a martyr, and he resembled the Prophet. It was narrated that Ibn Abbas was informed of the death of his brother Qutham while in his home, so he said 'Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi rajiun' and halted by the roadside, prayed two rak'ahs in which he prolonged the sitting, then stood up to his mount reciting: 'And seek help through patience and prayer, and indeed it is difficult except for the humble' (Quran 2:45). Qutham left no descendants. When the army was alarmed by the rumor that Quraysh had killed Uthman, the Prophet (peace be upon him) became angry and anxious and said: 'By Allah, if they have killed him, I will set it ablaze upon them with fire.' Then he took the Pledge of Ridwan from the Companions on account of this news and said: 'This is my left hand of Uthman, and it is better for him than his right hand.' So he was the cause of the Pledge of Ridwan and the anger of the Prophet (peace be upon him), so how can he be diminished by his delay from it? All that we have described demonstrates the virtue of Uthman, his innocence, his justice, the soundness of his allegiance, and that he was killed wrongfully.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two objections raised against Uthman by his detractors. The author, Baqillani, addresses each objection in turn, presenting arguments to vindicate Uthman's character and actions. The first objection is that Uthman did not participate in the Battle of Badr. Baqillani responds that at most this would imply that someone else is more excellent, but the imamate of the less excellent is permissible when the more excellent is hindered by a valid excuse. Moreover, Uthman's absence was specifically by the command of the Prophet himself, who ordered him to stay behind to care for his daughter Ruqayya, who was ill. The Prophet acknowledged his merit by giving him the share of booty of a participant. If Uthman had stayed behind without excuse, the Prophet would have blamed him, but he did not. The second objection concerns Uthman's absence from the Pledge of Ridwan (Bay'at al-Ridwan) at Hudaybiyya. Baqillani responds that Uthman had been sent by the Prophet as an envoy to the Quraysh in Mecca. The rumor of his murder sparked the Prophet's anger and led to the pledge. Thus, Uthman was the direct cause of this momentous event, and the Prophet symbolically included him by placing his left hand on his right. Baqillani concludes that all these facts prove Uthman's virtue, innocence, justice, and that he was killed unjustly. The passage weaves together historical reports and theological reasoning to defend Uthman against the allegations of his opponents.

Key Terms
بيعة الرضوان
الفضيلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Not being physically present at the pledge indicates Uthman was less devoted.
Correction: Uthman was on a prophetic mission, and his supposed death sparked the pledge itself.

Checkpoint
What event directly led to the Pledge of Ridwan according to Baqillani?
A) Uthman's arrival from Mecca.
B) The rumor that Quraysh had killed Uthman.
C) The Prophet's revelation.
D) A battle with Quraysh.

Key Takeaway
Uthman's role as envoy and the cause of the pledge elevates his status above those merely present.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a Companion like Uthman, do you immediately dismiss it as ignorance, or do you take time to learn the full story? Will you commit to defending the honor of the Companions with knowledge, not just emotion?
?
The Prophet honored Uthman's absence more than the presence of others. In your own life, do you seek recognition for visible service, or are you content to serve behind the scenes, knowing that Allah sees and honors even what others might overlook?
?
Baqillani calls the objection 'carelessness, ignorance, obstinacy, and stubbornness.' Which of these describes your attitude when you are presented with evidence that challenges a preconceived notion? Are you willing to let go of stubbornness and embrace the truth, even if it humbles you?

The Opening Argument for Ali's Imamate
Baqillani opens with a question and lists initial virtues.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani frames the discussion of Ali's imamate and the initial virtues he cites as proof.

Core Idea
Ali's imamate is argued through his complete virtues and precedence.

Baqillani begins a new chapter by posing the central question: what is the proof that Ali deserves the imamate? He immediately answers by listing Ali's unparalleled virtues—his early precedence, his struggles, his close relationship to the Prophet, and the famous hadiths in his praise. This passage sets the stage for the detailed arguments that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage twice: once for overall meaning, once while noting the key terms like 'السابقين الأولين' and 'الفضائل المشهورة'.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the full argument continues beyond this page.
2
Identify the question and answer structure
Notice how Baqillani presents the hypothetical objection and then provides the initial proof. This dialectical format is common in kalam.
3
List the virtues mentioned
From the answer, extract the specific virtues of Ali that are cited: being among the first Muslims, great jihad and service, close kinship, and the Prophet's praise (e.g., 'أقضاكم علي').
These virtues form the basis of the proof.
4
Understand the incomplete nature of the passage
Recognize that this passage only begins the proof; the conclusion is not included here. It is important to see that this is an introductory statement of evidence.
Further lessons will continue the argument.

باب الكلام في إمامة علي عليه السلام والرد على الواقف فيها والقادح في صحتها فإن قال قائل : ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عليّ وأنه أهل لما قام به وأسند إليه ومستحق لإمامة الأمة؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك كمال خلال الفضل فيه واجتماعها له لأنه من السابقين الأولين وممن كثر بلاؤه وجهاده في سبيل الله وعظم غناؤه في الإسلام وعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مع ما له من القرابة الخاصة وتزويجه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ابنته وكريمته فاطمة عليه السلام، وما روي فيه من الفضائل المشهورة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم نحو قوله : أقضاكم عليّ
Chapter on the discussion of the Imamate of Ali, peace be upon him, and refutation of the one who stops short (in affirming it) and the one who impugns its validity. So if someone says: What is the proof for establishing the Imamate of Ali and that he is worthy of what he assumed and was entrusted with and deserving of the leadership of the community? Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of a new section on the Imamate of Ali. Baqillani sets up the discussion by posing the question a hypothetical objector might ask: What is the proof that Ali is worthy of the imamate and that he was rightly entitled to it? The author then provides the initial answer, which is that Ali possesses a complete set of virtues, including being among the first to accept Islam, his extensive efforts and jihad, his great contributions to Islam, his close kinship with the Prophet (being his cousin and son-in-law), and the well-known hadiths of the Prophet praising him, such as 'Ali is the most judicious among you.' This passage is a statement of the argument that will be further elaborated in subsequent pages. It is incomplete here; the proof and conclusion continue beyond the page.

Conclusion on Uthman's Virtue
Concludes a preceding argument about Uthman's virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five affirmations that conclude the argument about Uthman's virtue and martyrdom.

Core Idea
Uthman's virtue, justice, sound allegiance, and wrongful death are affirmed through reasoned argument.

This short passage serves as the concluding summary of a longer argument defending Uthman's status. The author lists five key points established through previous reasoning. Understanding this conclusion helps clarify the Sunni position on Uthman's merit and sets the stage for further discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic sentence once, then its translation. Notice that it is a single concluding statement that lists multiple affirmations.
The word 'فدل' (so indicates) shows this is a result of prior reasoning.
2
Identify the five affirmations
The passage mentions five things: virtue (فضل), purity (نزاهة), justice (عدالة), soundness of allegiance (سلامة بيعته), and being killed wrongfully (قتل مظلوما). List them and consider what each means.
These are not random; they respond to specific historical accusations.
3
Reflect on the overall argument
Ask yourself: Why does the author conclude with these five points? How do they collectively defend Uthman's position in Islamic history?
This conclusion reinforces the Sunni view of Uthman as a rightly guided caliph and martyr.

Proofs for Ali's Imamate: Objection and Answer
Objection and multi-proof answer for Ali's imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses cumulative evidence (precedence, sacrifice, kinship, prophetic commendations) to prove Ali's imamate in the face of an objection.

Core Idea
Ali's imamate is proven by a convergence of virtues, not a single proof.

Imam Baqillani now defends the imamate of Ali by answering a hypothetical objection. The opponent asks for proof; the response does not rely on a single argument but stacks multiple lines of evidence—from Ali's early precedence to his knowledge and prophetic praise. This passage shows how classical kalam reasoned from established facts about a person to their fitness for leadership.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the chapter heading announces the topic of Ali's imamate and refutation of doubters.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to footnotes in the original; focus on the full argument given.
2
Identify the objection and answer structure
Find the hypothetical question 'What is the proof...' and then the answer beginning with 'الدليل على ذلك'. The answer then lists several evidences.
This is a classic objection-and-answer format common in kalam texts.
3
Examine each of the six evidences
Go through each evidence: 1) being among the earliest Muslims, 2) great struggle and jihad, 3) immense contribution to Islam, 4) special kinship to the Prophet, 5) marriage to Fatima, 6) well-known hadiths (judgment, love, banner).
Note how the author expands on the first hadith to explain that judgment implies comprehensive knowledge needed for an imam.
4
Reflect on the cumulative argument
Consider why the author presents multiple proofs rather than just one. How does each evidence support the claim that Ali is 'أهل' (worthy) for imamate?
The convergence of virtues makes the case stronger than any single proof alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إمامة علي عليه السلام والرد على الواقف فيها والقادح في صحتها
فإن قال قائل : ما الدليل على إثبات إمامة عليّ وأنه أهل لما قام به وأسند إليه ومستحق لإمامة الأمة؟ .
قيل له : الدليل على ذلك كمال خلال الفضل فيه واجتماعها له لأنه من السابقين الأولين وممن كثر بلاؤه وجهاده في سبيل الله وعظم غناؤه في الإسلام وعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مع ما له من القرابة الخاصة وتزويجه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ابنته وكريمته فاطمة عليه السلام، وما رُوي فيه من الفضائل المشهورة عن النبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم نحو قوله : «أقضاكم عليّ وأفرَضُكم زيد»؛ مع العلم بأن القضاء يشتمل على معرفة أبواب الحلال والحرام وأحكام الشرع وما يحتاج إلى علمه إمام الأمة؛ ونحو قوله : «حُبُّ عليّ إيمان وبغضه نفاق»؛ وقوله في خيبر : «لأدفعن الراية إلى رجل كرار غیر فرار يحب الله ورسوله ويحبه الله ورسوله» ودفع الراية إليه بعد أن تفل
Chapter on the discussion of the imamate of Ali, peace be upon him, and rebuttal of those who stop short of it or impugn its validity. For if someone says: What is the proof for establishing the imamate of Ali and that he is worthy of what he undertook and was entrusted with, and deserving of the imamate of the community? It is said to him: The proof for that is the completeness of the virtues in him and their coming together in him, because he is among the earliest forerunners, among those whose struggle and jihad in the path of God were great, and whose contribution to Islam and from the Messenger of God was immense, along with his special kinship and the Prophet's marriage to his noble daughter Fatima, peace be upon her, and the well-known virtues related from the Prophet, such as his saying: 'The most judicious among you is Ali, and the most knowledgeable of inheritance division is Zayd'; with the knowledge that jurisprudence encompasses knowledge of the categories of lawful and unlawful, the rulings of the Law, and what the imam of the community needs to know; and like his saying: 'Love of Ali is faith and hatred of him is hypocrisy'; and his saying at Khaybar: 'I will give the banner to a man who attacks and does not flee, who loves God and His Messenger and is loved by God and His Messenger,' and he gave him the banner after he had spit.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer proof for the imamate of Ali. The author begins with a chapter heading declaring the topic: discussion of Ali's imamate and refutation of those who deny or doubt its validity. Then comes the objection: a hypothetical question asking for the proof that Ali is worthy of the imamate. The answer provides several cumulative evidences. First, Ali is among the earliest Muslims (السابقين الأولين), indicating precedence in faith. Second, his struggle and jihad were great (كثر بلاؤه وجهاده). Third, his contribution to Islam and the Prophet was immense (عظم غناؤه في الإسلام وعن رسول الله). Fourth, his special kinship (القرابة الخاصة) — being the Prophet's cousin and son-in-law. Fifth, the Prophet married his daughter Fatima to him. Sixth, well-known hadiths of the Prophet: (a) 'The most judicious among you is Ali' — the author notes that jurisprudence (القضاء) includes knowledge of halal, haram, and all legal rulings needed by an imam, so this indicates Ali's comprehensive knowledge. (b) 'Love of Ali is faith and hatred is hypocrisy.' (c) At Khaybar, the Prophet said he would give the banner to a man who loves God and His Messenger and is loved by them, and then gave it to Ali after spitting (to heal his eyes). All these prove Ali's merit and thus his entitlement to the imamate.

السابقون الأولون

راية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think imamate is based solely on political power or hereditary succession without regard to virtue.
Correction: Baqillani argues that imamate is established through religious virtue, knowledge, and prophetic designation—not mere political power.

Key Takeaway
Ali's imamate is established through the convergence of his early precedence, immense jihad, kinship, and prophetic testimonials of his knowledge and faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that love of Ali is faith and hatred is hypocrisy. Do you truly feel love for Ali in your heart, or is it merely intellectual assent? What concrete action will you take this week to increase that love—such as reading his virtues, thanking Allah for him, or emulating his courage?
?
The proof of Ali's imamate is built on his actions and virtues, not just claims. If you were judged by your actions and virtues today, would you be found worthy of any leadership? What is the one area where your deeds fall short, and what will you do differently tomorrow to close that gap?
?
The Prophet honored Ali by marrying him to Fatima and testifying to his knowledge. How does your treatment of your own family reflect the honor you claim for the Prophetic household? Is there a family member you have neglected, and what is your commitment to mend that relationship starting today?

Love of Ali as a Sign of Faith
Author cites two hadiths on virtue of Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how two hadiths are used to demonstrate the high status of Ali ibn Abi Talib and that love of Ali is a sign of faith.

Core Idea
Love of Ali is a criterion of faith, hatred a sign of hypocrisy.

This lesson examines two hadiths presented by Imam al-Baqillani to support the virtue of Ali ibn Abi Talib. The first hadith highlights Zaid ibn Thabit's expertise in inheritance law, and the second directly states that love of Ali is faith. These narrations serve as evidence for the special station of Ali in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the literal translation to understand the basic meaning.
The passage is short but contains two separate hadith references.
2
Identify the two hadiths
Find the first hadith about Zaid's knowledge of inheritance (أفرضكم زيد) and the second about love of Ali being faith (حب علي إيمان).
The author introduces the second with 'ونحو قوله' meaning 'and similar to his saying'.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider what the second hadith implies: love of Ali is equated with faith, and hatred with hypocrisy. How does this support the author's argument about Ali's status?
This hadith does not mean love alone suffices for faith, but it is a strong sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفرَضُكم زيد؛ مع العلم بأن القضاء يشتمل على معرفة أبواب الحلال والحرام وأحكام الشرع وما يحتاج إلى علمه إمام الأمة؛ ونحو قوله : «حُبُّ عليّ إيمان وبغضه نفاق»

Commentary
This passage presents two hadiths as evidence for the virtues of Ali ibn Abi Talib. The first is a partial quote from a longer hadith that enumerates the most excellent in various fields: 'And the most knowledgeable of you in inheritance is Zaid.' The author then clarifies that judicial rulings require comprehensive knowledge of halal and haram and all Sharia rulings needed by the community's leader, thus showing the importance of such knowledge. The second hadith is a direct statement of the Prophet: 'Love of Ali is faith and hatred of him is hypocrisy.' This equates the inner disposition towards Ali with the core of belief itself, making love of Ali a criterion of faith and hatred a sign of hypocrisy. The author presents these as established truths, using them to support the high station of Ali.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'Love of Ali is faith' means that loving Ali alone is sufficient for complete faith.
Correction: The hadith indicates that love of Ali is a sign of faith, not the entirety of faith. It is a criterion among others, not a replacement for the fundamental beliefs and practices of Islam.

Love of Ali is a sign of faith, and hatred of him is a sign of hypocrisy, as taught by the Prophet.

?
You have just learned that the Prophet explicitly tied love of a Companion to faith itself. Does your claim to faith withstand this test? What will you do to ensure your love for Ali and the Ahl al-Bayt is genuine and active, not merely a lip service?

The Flag at Khaybar and Ali's Healing
Author recounts the Prophet giving the flag to Ali and the miracle of healing his eyes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Khaybar hadith demonstrates Ali's virtue and the Prophet's miracle, and why it does not imply prophethood for Ali.

Core Idea
The Prophet's miracle through Ali highlights honor, not divinity.

This passage presents a well-known event from the Battle of Khaybar, where the Prophet bestows a banner on Ali with a special description and then performs a healing miracle. The narrative serves as a testimony to Ali's high rank and the authenticity of prophetic miracles. As we read, notice how the language emphasizes both Ali's qualities and the Prophet's miraculous act.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the wording. The terms 'karrār' and 'ghayr firār' are key descriptors of Ali's bravery.
The phrase 'karrār ghayr firār' is a famous praise meaning one who attacks repeatedly and never retreats.
2
Translate and understand the narrative
Read the literal translation. Identify the three parts: the Prophet's statement, the act of giving the banner with the healing miracle, and Ali's testimony.
3
Analyze the miracle
Focus on the miracle: the Prophet spat in Ali's sore eyes and they were healed permanently. This is a clear prophetic miracle (karama) associated with Ali.
This miracle is a sign of Ali's virtue and the Prophet's truthfulness, not a proof of Ali's prophethood.
4
Address the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding: some might think this proves Ali had a special divine status. The passage only shows his love for Allah and the Prophet's miracle, not prophethood.
The lesson guards against exaggerating Ali's rank beyond that of a Companion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage presents another virtue of Ali: the event at the Battle of Khaybar. The Prophet declared that he would give the military standard to a man characterized by bravery ('one who attacks and does not flee') and mutual love with Allah and the Messenger. This description is applied to Ali. The Prophet then gave the banner to Ali after performing a miracle: he spat into Ali's eyes, which were inflamed with ophthalmia, and Ali was immediately cured. Ali himself testifies that his eyes never ached again. Thus, the hadith demonstrates Ali's high rank and a clear miracle (karama) associated with the Prophet's action.

?

The Meaning of 'Mawla' in the Hadith of Ghadir
Baqillani interprets the 'Man kuntu mawlahu' hadith and defines 'mawla' as 'helper'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani argues that 'mawla' in the hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' means 'helper' and not 'master' or 'successor', and how this supports Ali's authority as a helper of the nation.

Core Idea
Mawla means helper, not master — but that still implies great authority.

Imam al-Baqillani tackles a key hadith often cited in discussions about leadership. The Prophet's declaration at Ghadir Khumm has been interpreted in various ways. Here, the author focuses on the linguistic meaning of 'mawla' to clarify the nature of Ali's relationship to the community. He argues that 'mawla' means 'helper' and 'assistant', using Quranic and poetic evidence, but still affirms that this establishes Ali's special duty to support and guide the nation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Read the Arabic passage that begins with the Prophet's statement 'Man kuntu mawlahu fa Ali mawlahu' after he asked about his own authority. Notice how the author ties the concept of mawla to the earlier statement of awla (more entitled).
2
Examine the linguistic argument
The author claims that 'mawla' means 'nasir' (helper) by consensus of language experts. Look at the Quran verse and the poetry he cites. Ask: why does he argue so strongly for this meaning?
3
Reflect on the implications
If 'mawla' means helper, then the hadith establishes Ali as the helper of the ummah. The author says this imposes an obligation of allegiance (muwalat) both inwardly and outwardly. What does that tell us about Ali's status?
This is not a political appointment, but a spiritual and practical duty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : «من كنت مولاه فعلي مولاه» بعد قوله : ألستُ أولى بالمؤمنين من أنفسهم؟» فأوجب من موالاته على باطنه وظاهره والقطع على طهارة سريرته ما أثبته لنفسه وأعلمهم أن عَلِيّاً ناصِرٌ للأمة مجاهد في سبيل الله بظاهره وباطنه; لأن المولى يكون بمعنى الناصر المُعِين باتفاق أهل اللغة قال الله تعالى : فإن الله مولاه وجبريل وصالح المؤمنين يعني ناصره : وقال الأخطل : فأصبحت مولاها من الناس كلهم وأحرى قريش أن تُهابَ وتحمدا يعني أصبحت ناصرها من الناس يعني عبد الملك بن مروان; لأن أحداً في وقته لم يقدر على مثل نُصرته ; إذ كان إمامهم إذ ذاك وقائدهم وإن كان فيهم ناصر دونه . ومن فضائله قوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم ، في غزاة تبوك لما لحق به وشكا خوض الناس في بابه: «أما ترضى أن تكون مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى ، إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي» أي : إني استخلفك على المدينة كمـا
And his saying: 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' after his saying: 'Am I not more entitled to the believers than themselves?' So he made incumbent from his allegiance inwardly and outwardly and the certainty of the purity of his inner self what he had established for himself, and he informed them that Ali is a helper of the nation, striving in the path of Allah outwardly and inwardly; because al-mawla carries the meaning of the helper, the assistant, by agreement of the people of language. Allah the Exalted said: 'For indeed Allah is his Mawla, and Jibril, and the righteous believers' (Quran 66:4), meaning his helper. And al-Akhtal said: 'So I became its mawla from all the people, and Quraysh are more deserving to be feared and praised' meaning he became its helper from the people, meaning Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan; because no one in his time was capable of similar assistance, as he was their imam and leader at that time, even if there were helpers below him. And among his virtues is his saying, peace be upon him, in the expedition of Tabuk when he caught up with him and complained about people's gossip regarding his household: 'Are you not pleased to be from me in the station of Harun from Musa, except that there is no prophet after me?' meaning: I appoint you as my successor over Medina just as...
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage examines two major hadiths about Ali. First, the 'Man kuntu mawlahu' hadith: after the Prophet asked the people if he was not more entitled (awla) to the believers than themselves, he declared that whoever accepts him as mawla should accept Ali as mawla. The author argues that this imposes an obligation of allegiance (muwalat) to Ali both inwardly and outwardly, and establishes certainty about the purity of his inner state. The author then explains the meaning of 'mawla' by citing linguistic consensus: it means 'helper' (nasir) and 'assistant' (mu'in). This is supported by Quran 66:4, where Allah is called the Mawla of the Prophet, meaning helper, and by a line of poetry from al-Akhtal where 'mawla' clearly means helper. The author uses this to argue that Ali is the helper of the nation and a mujahid in Allah's path. Second, the hadith of the station of Harun: the Prophet told Ali during Tabuk, 'Are you not pleased to be from me in the station of Harun from Musa, except that there is no prophet after me?' This is interpreted as the Prophet appointing Ali as his successor over Medina, just as Harun was Musa's deputy. The passage thus presents these hadiths as proofs of Ali's special authority and virtue.

Key Terms
المولى
الناصر
الموالاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'mawla' in this hadith means 'master' or 'successor', implying political succession.
Correction: Baqillani argues that 'mawla' means 'helper' as proven by linguistic evidence, not master. However, the helper role still implies a high status.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'mawla' in the hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' as established by the author?
A) Master and owner.
B) Friend and beloved.
C) Helper and assistant.
D) Successor and caliph.

Key Takeaway
The word 'mawla' means 'helper' in this hadith, establishing Ali's duty to aid the Muslim community, not necessarily political succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the hadith of Ghadir, do you feel a personal responsibility toward Ali (ra) as your helper (nasir)? What would it mean for you to truly accept him as a helper who guides the ummah, and how would that change your attitude toward his legacy today?
?
The Prophet (saw) first asked, 'Am I not more entitled to the believers than themselves?' before declaring Ali as mawla. If you truly believe that the Prophet (saw) has authority over you, does that authority extend to those he designated as helpers after him? What is one concrete way you can submit to that authority this week?
?
The author argues that 'mawla' means helper, but the helper is also a leader. Are you content to be a passive follower, or do you actively see yourself as a helper (nasir) of the truth? What is one step you can take today to become a stronger helper for your community in the path of Allah?

The Station of Harun: Ali as Successor to the Prophet
Baqillani cites the hadith of the station of Harun to show Ali's virtue as successor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'You are to me as Harun was to Musa, except no prophet after me' establishes Ali's appointment as the Prophet's successor over Medina and its implications for his authority.

Core Idea
Ali is to the Prophet as Harun was to Musa: a deputy, except prophethood.

The second hadith discussed by Imam al-Baqillani is the famous statement made during the expedition of Tabuk. When Ali complained about gossip, the Prophet reassured him by comparing his position to that of Harun (Aaron) to Musa (Moses). This hadith is often used to argue for Ali's right to succession. The author presents it as a proof of Ali's virtues, focusing on the idea of deputyship.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its occasion
Read the Arabic passage describing the event of Tabuk: Ali caught up with the Prophet and complained about people's talk. The Prophet responded with the hadith of the station of Harun.
2
Understand the analogy
The Prophet compares himself to Musa and Ali to Harun. Recall that Harun was Musa's brother and deputy while Musa was on Mount Sinai. What does this imply about Ali's role?
Except that no prophet comes after Muhammad.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'station'
The phrase 'station of Harun' suggests appointing Ali as successor over Medina during the Prophet's absence. How does this support the idea of Ali's authority?
The author explicitly says 'I appoint you as my successor over Medina'.

The Meaning of 'Mawla' in the Hadith of Ghadir
Baqillani argues that 'mawla' means helper using Quran and poetry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Baqillani argues the word 'mawla' in the Ghadir hadith means 'helper' (nasir), not 'master' or 'successor', based on linguistic and textual evidence.

Core Idea
The word 'mawla' means helper, not master, in the hadith of Ghadir.

Imam Baqillani addresses a key sectarian dispute by clarifying the meaning of the word 'mawla' in the famous Ghadir hadith. He argues that the Prophet's statement is about Ali's role as a helper and protector, not about political succession. This lesson examines his linguistic reasoning and the evidence he provides from the Quran and classical poetry.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author’s own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with an anecdote about Ali’s eyes.
2
Identify the two pieces of evidence
Baqillani gives two proofs for the meaning of 'mawla' as helper: a Quranic verse and a line of poetry. Locate both in the text.
The Quranic verse is from Surah Tahrim, verse 4.
3
Understand the Quranic evidence
Examine the Quranic verse where 'mawla' is used for Allah, Jibril, and the righteous believers. Baqillani explains it means 'helper'.
This is a standard interpretation among classical scholars.
4
Understand the poetic evidence
Read the line of poetry by Al-Akhtal. Baqillani explains that 'mawla' here means 'helper', referring to Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan.
Poetry is used as evidence for linguistic usage.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this interpretation matters: it shows that the hadith is about Ali’s role as a helper of the Ummah, not about political succession.
This counters claims that the hadith designates Ali as the immediate successor.

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs for Ali's virtue. First, the author mentions a brief anecdote: when Ali's eyes were sore, he said they never became sore after that (possibly after a treatment by the Prophet). Then he cites the famous hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu fa Ali mawlahu'. The author argues that the word 'mawla' here means 'helper' (nasir), not 'master' or 'lord'. The Prophet's prior statement 'Am I not more entitled to the believers than their own selves?' establishes his authority, and then he says 'Whoever I am his mawla, Ali is his mawla' — meaning just as I am their helper and protector, so Ali is their helper and protector. The author supports this interpretation with two pieces of evidence: (1) the Quranic verse 'Indeed, Allah is his mawla, and Gabriel, and the righteous believers' where 'mawla' means helper, as in the interpretation of the scholars. (2) The poetry of Al-Akhtal, where 'mawla' is used to mean helper. The author explains the line: the poet says 'she became her mawla among all people' meaning she became her helper, referring to Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan. So the linguistic usage confirms that mawla can mean helper. Thus, the hadith establishes Ali's role as a helper and protector of the Ummah, not a divinely appointed successor in a political sense (as some sects might claim).

Key Terms
المولى
الناصر
الموالاة
الولاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret 'mawla' in the Ghadir hadith as 'master' or 'political successor' to Ali.
Correction: Baqillani shows through linguistic evidence that 'mawla' means 'helper', not 'master', so the hadith establishes Ali's role as a protector of the community, not a designated ruler.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what does the word 'mawla' mean in the hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu'?
A) Master (sayyid)
B) Helper (nasir)
C) Friend (sadiq)
D) Relative (qarib)

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu' establishes Ali as a helper and protector of the Muslim community, not a political successor, as proven by the linguistic meaning of 'mawla'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the hadith 'Man kuntu mawlahu', do you feel a personal call to actively help your community, or do you treat it as a historical footnote? What one concrete action will you take this week to be a 'nasir' for someone in need?
?
Baqillani relies on linguistic evidence to interpret the hadith correctly. How often do you rush to interpret Quran and hadith based on your own desires rather than humbly learning from those who know the language? Will you commit to studying Arabic so that you can understand Allah's words as intended?
?
The Prophet informed the companions that Ali is a helper. Are you a helper to your fellow believers in your home, mosque, or neighborhood? What is one habit you need to change to become a true supporter of others, not just a passive participant in your faith?

Ali's Rank as Deputy: The Hadith of Position
Baqillani cites the hadith equating Ali's position to that of Harun relative to Musa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of the Hadith of Position in establishing Ali's rank as the Prophet's deputy, while clarifying that prophethood ended with Muhammad (saw).

Core Idea
Ali's status mirrors Harun's, but without prophethood.

Imam Baqillani presents another virtue of Ali ibn Abi Talib: the Prophet's words during the Tabuk expedition. This hadith is often cited in discussions about Ali's rank and succession, but it also contains an important exception that guards against exaggeration. Let's examine the hadith and its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic hadith and its literal translation. Get a feel for the language and the context.
Notice the phrase 'except that there is no prophet after me'.
2
Understand the context
The hadith was said during the Tabuk expedition when Ali caught up and complained about gossip. Why did the Prophet say this?
The context helps explain why the Prophet emphasized deputyship.
3
Identify the key elements
Identify the deputyship (استخلاف) and the exception. What does this tell us about Ali's role?
The exception is crucial to prevent misunderstanding.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Think about why the Prophet explicitly said 'no prophet after me'. What does this clarify about prophethood and succession?
This hadith is used in debates about the caliphate and Ali's status.
5
Connect to broader discussion
Consider how this hadith fits into the larger discussion of Ali's virtues and the Sunni-Shia perspectives.
Baqillani uses it as evidence for Ali's high rank.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فضائله قوله صلى الله عليه وسلّم ، في غزاة تبوك لما لحق به وشكا خوض الناس في بابه: «أما ترضى أن تكون مني بمنزلة هارون من موسى ، إلا أنه لا نبي بعدي» (٤) ، أي : إني استخلفك على المدينة كمـا استخلف موسى أخاه هارون لما توجه لكلام ربه من غير بغض ولا قلى
And among his virtues is his statement, peace and blessings be upon him, during the expedition of Tabuk, when (Ali) caught up with him and complained about the people's gossip regarding him: 'Are you not pleased that you are to me as Harun was to Musa, except that there is no prophet after me?' i.e., I have appointed you as my deputy over Medina just as Musa appointed his brother Harun as deputy when he went to the speaking of his Lord, without any hatred or displeasure.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage presents another virtue of Ali: the Prophet's statement to him during the Battle of Tabuk. Ali had remained behind in Medina by the Prophet's order, and some people gossiped about him. When he caught up, he complained, and the Prophet said: 'Are you not pleased that you are to me as Harun was to Musa, except that there is no prophet after me?' The author explains: The Prophet meant that he appointed Ali as his deputy over Medina just as Musa appointed Harun as his deputy when he went to Mount Sinai. The phrase 'without any hatred or displeasure' indicates that the deputyship was pure and without any negative feelings. This hadith establishes Ali's elevated status as the Prophet's deputy and successor in his absence, comparable to Harun's role, but with the clear exclusion of prophethood after the Prophet.

Key Terms
المنزلة
الاستخلاف
هارون
موسى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the hadith implies prophethood for Ali.
Correction: The hadith explicitly excludes prophethood with the phrase 'except that there is no prophet after me', confirming the finality of Muhammad's prophethood.

Checkpoint

B) Uhud

D) Hunayn

Key Takeaway
The Hadith of Position elevates Ali to a status comparable to Harun, but the explicit exclusion of prophethood after Muhammad prevents overstatement of his role.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Ali Chosen to Deliver Surah Bara'ah
Baqillani cites hadith of Ali's delivery of Surah Bara'ah as proof of his merit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet specifically chose Ali to deliver Surah Bara'ah and what this indicates about Ali's status and trustworthiness.

Core Idea
Only a man from the Prophet himself could deliver a message of such weight.

This passage from Baqillani draws on a famous hadith to highlight a unique virtue of Ali. The Prophet's statement that only a man from him can convey on his behalf is realized when Ali is sent to recite Surah Bara'ah to the polytheists of Quraysh. Let's examine this proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the two parts: the prophetic statement and the application. The verse reference is from Surah Zukhruf.
2
Identify the key phrases
Identify 'None can convey on my behalf except a man from me' and the description of Quraysh as 'a contentious people'. Consider why these details are significant.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why was Ali chosen? What does this say about his character and role? Connect this to the broader argument about prophethood and virtue.
This connects to sectarian discussions about Ali's status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : لا يُؤدِّي عني إلا رجل مني» (١) ، وإنفاذه بسورة براءة يقرؤها على المشركين بمكة (۲)؛ وهذا أمر لا يليه إلا أهل القَدْرِ والنباهة ومن يصلح للتحمل والأداء عن رسول الله صلّى الله عليه وسلم إلى مثل قريش مع وفارة عقولهم وصحة أحلامهم وما وصفهم الله به فقال: بل هم قوم خصمون (٢) .
And his statement: 'None can convey on my behalf except a man from me' (1), and his sending him (Ali) with Surah Bara'ah to recite it to the polytheists in Mecca (2). This is a matter that only people of high status and intelligence can undertake, and those who are fit to bear and convey from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, to people like Quraysh, given their abundant intellect and sound judgment, and what Allah described them with: 'Nay, they are a contentious people' (Surah Zukhruf: 58).
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage cites another virtue: the Prophet's statement that only a man from his own family (or from him) can deliver a message on his behalf. This was realized when the Prophet sent Ali to recite Surah Bara'ah (the declaration of disavowal) to the polytheists in Mecca. The author comments that this task is only entrusted to people of high status and intelligence, who are capable of conveying the message to a people as articulate and contentious as Quraysh, whom Allah described as a 'contentious people'. This highlights Ali's unique ability and trustworthiness.

Key Terms

The Prophet's statement and action demonstrate that only a worthy person from his own family could deliver a message as critical as Surah Bara'ah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophet said 'none can convey on my behalf except a man from me.' What does it mean for you to be 'from' the Prophet in your daily conduct? Is your character such that you could be trusted with a divine message without distortion?
?
Ali was chosen for this task because of his high status and capability. Are you actively developing the intelligence, sound judgment, and spiritual depth required to serve Allah's cause, or are you content with remaining spiritually immature?

Ali's Virtue: The Hadith to Fatima and the Bird
Baqillani cites two hadiths showing Ali's high status with Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two prophetic hadiths that highlight Ali's high status with Allah, as presented by Baqillani.

Core Idea
Allah chose Ali alongside the Prophet as the best of creation.

Baqillani continues to support the virtues of Ali by citing specific incidents from the Prophet's life. In this passage, he presents two hadiths: one where the Prophet consoles Fatima by telling her that Allah chose her father and husband from all humanity, and another where the Prophet prays for the most beloved creature to Allah to share his meal, and Ali arrives. Both illustrate Ali's exceptional rank.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording come through before you interpret.
Note that the second hadith is incomplete in the source, ending with 'min'.
2
Understand the first hadith
The Prophet told Fatima that Allah looked at the people of the earth and chose two men: her father (the Prophet) and her husband (Ali). This shows Ali's high rank alongside the Prophet.
3
Understand the second hadith
The Prophet prayed for the most beloved creature to Allah to come eat with him, and Ali came. This indicates Ali is the most beloved to Allah.
The hadith is famous as 'Hadith al-Tair' and is often cited for Ali's virtue.
4
Reflect on the author's purpose
Baqillani uses these hadiths to further establish Ali's virtues in the context of sectarian discussions about the caliphate and the superiority of the Companions.

ومن فضائله قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لفاطمة، وقد شكت له بعض حالها: «أما ترضين أن الله قد اطلع على أهل الأرض فاختار منهم رجلين جعل أحدهم أباك وجعل الآخر بعلك؟» (۳). وقوله صلّى الله عليه وسلم: «اللهم انتني بأحب الخلق إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطائر» (٤) ، فجاء علي فأكل معه من

(3). And his statement, peace be upon him: 'O Allah, bring to me the most beloved of creation to you to eat with me from this bird' (4). So Ali came and ate with him from it.

Commentary
This passage presents two additional hadiths showing Ali's virtue. First, the Prophet comforted Fatima by informing her that Allah had chosen two men from all people on earth: her father (the Prophet) and her husband (Ali). This indicates Ali's high rank alongside the Prophet. Second, the incident of the bird: the Prophet prayed that the most beloved creature to Allah would come to eat with him, and Ali came. This shows Ali's special status as the most beloved to Allah. The author uses these to further establish Ali's virtues.

The Evidence for Ali's Caliphate
Baqillani presents an objection and answers with historical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical evidence Baqillani uses to defend the legitimacy of ʿAlī's caliphate and how it addresses an objection.

Core Idea
The Companions' reluctant offer under threat proves the validity of Ali's caliphate.

Baqillani anticipates an objection: even if ʿAlī was virtuous, was his caliphate contractually valid? He responds by recounting the historical events after ʿUthmān's murder, showing that the Companions were forced by circumstances to offer the caliphate, and that ʿAlī's acceptance was necessary to end the fitna. This lesson examines that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Identify the question the objector asks: what is the evidence that the contract for ʿAlī was valid?
2
Read the answer
Follow the historical narrative: why did the Companions act to appoint an imam after ʿUthmān's death?
Note the threat from al-Ghāfiqī and the people of fitna.
3
Note the three refusals
Examine the poetic refusals of ʿAlī, Ṭalḥa, and az-Zubayr. What do these show about their reluctance?
Each refused, indicating the caliphate was not sought.
4
Understand the point
How does this narrative prove the validity of ʿAlī's caliphate? Consider the Companions' consensus and the urgency of ending the fitna.
The conclusion is cut off in the source, but the argument is that the caliphate was imposed by necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما الدليل مع ما ذكرتم من فضله وجلالة قدره وصلاحه لهذا الأمر على أن العقد له وقع موقعاً صحيحاً يجب الانقياد لصاحبه والاقتداء به؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أن عثمان رضي الله عنه لما قُتِلَ استولى الغافِقِيُّ ومن صار معه من أهل الفتنة على المدينة وهموا بالفتك بأهلها وحلفوا على ذلك للصحابة متى لم يُقَدِّمُوا النظر في أمرهم ويعقدوا الإمامة لرجل منهم فأراد الصحابة حسم مادة الفتنة وعُرِضَ هذا الأمر على عليّ عليه السلام والتمس منه وآثره المصريون فامتنع عليهم وأعظم قتل عثمان وأنشأ يقول : ولو أن قومي طاوعتني سَرَاتُهم أمرتهم أمراً يُديخ الأعاديا ولزم بيته . ثم عُرِضَ ذلك على طلحة وآثره البصريون، وأبى ذلك وكرهه وأنشأ يقول : ومن عجب الأيام والدهر أنني بقيت وحيداً لا أمر ولا أخلي ثم عُرِض ذلك على الزبير فأبى وأنشأ يقول : متى أنت عن دار بفيحان راحل وباعتها تخني عليه الكتائب وأعلى المربد حجارة رخوة، وهو الموضع الذي يسمى الحزيز.
If a questioner says: What is the evidence, along with what you have mentioned of his virtue, the majesty of his rank, and his suitability for this matter, that the contract (al-ʿaqd) for him occurred validly, such that submission to its possessor and following him is obligatory? It is said to him: The evidence for that is that when ʿUthmān, may Allah be pleased with him, was killed, al-Ghāfiqī and those with him from the people of tribulation (ahl al-fitna) took control of Medina and intended to kill its people, and they swore to the Companions (aṣ-Ṣaḥāba) that if they did not proceed to consider their affair and contract the imamate (al-imāma) for one of them, [they would do so]. So the Companions wanted to cut off the root of tribulation, and this matter was presented to ʿAlī, peace be upon him, and he was asked, and the Egyptians preferred him, but he refused them, magnified the killing of ʿUthmān, and recited: 'If my people's leaders had obeyed me, I would have commanded them a command that humiliates the enemies' and he stayed in his house. Then it was presented to Ṭalḥa, and the Basrans preferred him, but he refused and disliked it and recited: 'Among the wonders of days and time is that I remain alone, neither commanding nor leaving.' Then it was presented to az-Zubayr, and he refused and recited: 'When will you depart from the house of Bafīḥān, O traveler? Its palm trees afflict him with the battalions.' And the top of al-Mirbad is soft stones, and it is the place called al-Ḥazīz.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument. The objector acknowledges the virtues of ʿAlī that were just listed but asks for the specific evidence (al-dalīl) that the contract (al-ʿaqd) of his caliphate was valid and binding. The answer provides a historical narrative: after ʿUthmān's murder, a faction (al-Ghāfiqī and the people of fitna) seized Medina and threatened to kill the Companions unless they appointed an imam. To prevent chaos, the Companions sought a willing candidate. They first offered the caliphate to ʿAlī, who refused out of reverence for ʿUthmān's blood. Then they offered it to Ṭalḥa, who also refused, and then to az-Zubayr, who likewise refused. The narrative includes lines of poetry each recited to express their reluctance. The point of the evidence is that the caliphate was imposed on ʿAlī by necessity to avert greater evil, and his eventual acceptance was legitimate because it was the collective decision of the Companions under duress. The explanatory note about 'al-Mirbad' identifies a location. The answer is cut off in the window, but the argument shows that the validity of ʿAlī's caliphate rests on the historical circumstances of the Companions' consensus and the urgency of ending the fitna.

Key Terms
الدليل (al-dalīl)
العقد (al-ʿaqd)
الإمامة (al-imāma)
الفتنة (al-fitna)
الصحابة (aṣ-Ṣaḥāba)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that ʿAlī's caliphate was merely a political power grab.
Correction: Baqillani argues it was a reluctant acceptance forced by circumstances to preserve the community, as shown by the Companions' repeated offers and refusals.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the evidence for the validity of ʿAlī's caliphate?
A) ʿAlī's superior knowledge and virtue
B) The Companions' collective offer to him under threat of fitna
C) A direct command from the Prophet
D) ʿAlī's own desire for power

Key Takeaway
The validity of ʿAlī's caliphate is evidenced by the Companions' collective offer to him under duress, which he reluctantly accepted to end the fitna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions offered the caliphate to ʿAlī, Ṭalḥa, and az-Zubayr, all of whom refused out of reverence for ʿUthmān's blood. When have you refused a duty out of principle, and when have you accepted it for the greater good? What does your response reveal about your priorities?
?
If you were in the position of the Companions under threat of violence, would you have insisted on a candidate who was reluctant, or would you have chosen someone eager for power? Why? This passage shows that legitimate authority can be forced by circumstances—how does that challenge your view of leadership?
?
The people of fitna used violence to pressure the Companions into appointing an imam. Have you ever made a decision under pressure that you later regretted? How can you ensure your choices are driven by sincerity (ikhlāṣ) rather than fear or convenience?

The Evidence for the Soundness of Ali's Bay'ah
Baqillani proves the validity of Ali's caliphate with historical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical and rational evidence for the validity of Ali ibn Abi Talib's caliphate as presented by Imam Baqillani.

Core Idea
Ali's caliphate was valid because it was a necessity to prevent fitna, accepted by the most qualified Companions.

Baqillani anticipates an objection: what proof is there that Ali's bay'ah was valid? He responds by recounting the events after Uthman's murder, showing that the Companions acted out of necessity and that Ali was the most deserving. This passage establishes the Sunni position on the legitimacy of Ali's caliphate.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opening question: someone asks for evidence that the contract of bay'ah for Ali was sound and binding.
This sets up the need for a proof.
2
Follow the historical narrative
Learn the sequence: after Uthman's death, the rebels (ahl al-fitna) took control of Medina and threatened its people unless a leader was appointed.
The Companions acted to prevent bloodshed.
3
Note the refusals of Ali, Talha, and Zubayr
All three initially refused the caliphate out of reverence for Uthman, showing their reluctance.
This counters claims of eagerness for power.
4
See the necessity and consensus
When the rebels intensified threats, the senior Companions implored Ali to accept, and he did only after seeing it as a benefit. The bay'ah was conducted by qualified individuals like Khuzayma and Ammar.
The conclusion: this bay'ah is among the soundest contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما الدليل مع ما ذكرتم من فضله وجلالة قدره وصلاحه لهذا الأمر على أن العقد له وقع موقعاً صحيحاً يجب الانقياد لصاحبه والاقتداء به؟ قيل له : الدليل على ذلك أن عثمان رضي الله عنه لما قُتِلَ استولى الغافِقِيُّ ومن صار معه من أهل الفتنة على المدينة وهموا بالفتك بأهلها وحلفوا على ذلك للصحابة متى لم يُقَدِّمُوا النظر في أمرهم ويعقدوا الإمامة لرجل منهم فأراد الصحابة حسم مادة الفتنة وعُرِضَ هذا الأمر على عليّ عليه السلام والتمس منه وآثره المصريون فامتنع عليهم وأعظم قتل عثمان وأنشأ يقول : ولو أن قومي طاوعتني سَرَاتُهم أمرتهم أمراً يُديخ الأعاديا ولزم بيته . ثم عُرِضَ ذلك على طلحة وآثره البصريون، وأبى ذلك وكرهه. ثم عُرِض ذلك على الزبير فأبى. كل ذلك منهم إنكار لقتل عثمان وإعظام له ورزية به. فلما حلف أهل الفتنة على الفتك بأهل المدينة وإلقاح الفتنة وردها جَذَعة، اجتمع وجـوه المهاجرين والأنصار عشية اليوم الثالث على ما رُوي من قتل عثمان فسألوا علياً هذا الأمر وأقسموا عليه فيه وناشدوه الله في حفظ بقية الأمة وصيانة دار الهجرة فدخل في ذلك بعد شدة وبعد أن رآه مصلحة، ورأى القوم ذلك لعلمهم وعلمه بأنه أعلم من بقي وأفضلهم وأولاهم بهذا الأمر، فمد يده وبايعه جماعةُ من حَضَرَ منهم خزيمة بن ثابت، وأبو الهيثم بن التيهان، ومحمد بن مسلمة، وعمار في رجال يكثر عددهم من المهاجرين والأنصار وهذا من أصح العقود وأثبتها لأن المعقود له أفضل من بقي ومن ذكرناه من العاقدين بصفة من يملك عقد الإمامة في الفضل والسابقة فوجب بذلك تمام بيعته وصحة إمامته
If someone says: What is the evidence, along with what you have mentioned of his virtue, his high status, and his suitability for this matter, that the contract for him took place in a sound manner, making it obligatory to submit to its owner and follow him? It is said to him: The evidence for that is that when Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, was killed, al-Ghafiqiyy and those with him from the people of fitna took control of Medina and intended to kill its people, and they swore to do that unless the Companions advanced the consideration of their affair and contracted the imamate for a man among them. So the Companions wanted to cut off the root of fitna. This matter was presented to Ali, peace be upon him, and he was requested, and the Egyptians preferred him, but he refused them, magnified the killing of Uthman, and composed: 'If my people's leaders had obeyed me, I would have commanded them a command that humiliates the enemies' and he stayed in his house. Then it was presented to Talha, and the Basrans preferred him, but he refused and disliked it. Then it was presented to al-Zubayr, and he refused. All of that from them was denial of the killing of Uthman, veneration of him, and calamity due to him. So when the people of fitna swore to kill the people of Medina and to ignite fitna and return it fresh, the prominent Muhajirun and Ansar gathered on the evening of the third day according to what was narrated of the killing of Uthman, and they asked Ali for this matter, adjured him, and implored him by Allah to preserve the rest of the Ummah and protect the abode of Hijrah. So he entered into it after hardship and after he saw it as a benefit, and the people saw that due to their knowledge and his knowledge that he was the most knowledgeable of those remaining, their most virtuous, and the most entitled to this matter. So he extended his hand, and a group of those present gave him bay'ah, among them Khuzayma ibn Thabit, Abu al-Haytham ibn al-Tayyahan, Muhammad ibn Maslama, and Ammar, and men whose number was many from the Muhajirun and Ansar. This is among the soundest and strongest contracts, because the one contracted for is the most virtuous of those remaining, and those we mentioned among the contractors are qualified to contract the imamah in virtue and precedence. So by that, the completion of his bay'ah and the validity of his imamate are established.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the validity of Ali ibn Abi Talib's caliphate. It begins with a hypothetical objection: given the virtues of Ali already mentioned, what is the evidence that the actual contract of bay'ah was sound and binding? The author responds by recounting the historical circumstances after the murder of Uthman. The people of fitna (the rebels) had taken over Medina and threatened to kill the inhabitants unless the Companions appointed a leader. To prevent greater bloodshed and fitna, the Companions offered the caliphate first to Ali, who refused out of reverence for Uthman. Then they offered it to Talha and al-Zubayr, who also refused. All three displayed their grief over Uthman's death. When the rebels insisted on their demand, the senior Muhajirun and Ansar gathered and implored Ali to accept, appealing to him by Allah to preserve the Ummah. Ali accepted only after seeing it as a necessary benefit. The key point is that the bay'ah was carried out by the most qualified men (Khuzayma, Abu al-Haytham, Muhammad ibn Maslama, Ammar, and many others) who were themselves qualified to contract the imamah due to their virtue and precedence. The author concludes that because Ali was the best among the remaining Companions and the contractors were qualified, the bay'ah was among the soundest contracts, and its validity is established.

الانقياد
الاقتداء

الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's caliphate was invalid because he initially refused and because later claims of coercion existed.
Correction: The passage shows his initial refusal was out of reverence for Uthman, and he only accepted when forced by necessity and the consensus of the senior Companions.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what was the primary reason the Companions pressed Ali to accept the caliphate?
A) Ali was the most deserving and they wanted to honor him
B) They feared the people of fitna would kill the people of Medina if no leader was appointed
C) Talha and al-Zubayr refused, leaving no other option
D) The people of Egypt forced them to choose Ali

Key Takeaway
Ali's bay'ah was valid because it was a necessity to prevent fitna, led by the most virtuous Companions, and accepted by the most deserving candidate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you accepted a difficult responsibility only after being pressed by others, and how did that align with or violate your own initial judgment? Are there situations where you are currently avoiding a responsibility that Allah may be placing on you through the needs of others?
?
The Companions prioritised preventing fitna over personal comfort. Is there an area of your life where you are choosing peace over taking a necessary stand, or conversely, choosing confrontation when reconciliation is more virtuous?
?
If the most qualified person for a role in your community is not you, would you actively support and elevate that person, even at the cost of your own ambition? How does your heart truly react when others are chosen over you?

Refutation of Coerced Bay'ah Objections to Ali's Caliphate
Baqillani refutes claims that Ali's bay'ah was invalid due to coercion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that the alleged coercion of Talha and al-Zubayr does not invalidate Ali's caliphate, and how he addresses each narrated objection.

Core Idea
A valid bay'ah establishes the imamate; later events cannot undo it.

Baqillani responds to critics who claim that Ali's caliphate is invalid because Talha and al-Zubayr were forced to pledge allegiance. He explains that the bay'ah had already been completed by other qualified Companions, so subsequent coercion does not affect its validity. In this passage, he systematically refutes each narrated objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first paragraph which presents the opponent's case: narrations that Talha and al-Zubayr were brought forcibly to pledge allegiance to Ali, implying that the bay'ah was invalid.
Notice the multiple details: the withered hand, the condition to kill Uthman's killers, and the claim of coercion.
2
Understand Baqillani's main argument
In the second paragraph, Baqillani asserts that the bay'ah had already been completed by other Companions before Talha and al-Zubayr participated. Thus, their later coerced pledge does not affect the already established imamate.
He uses analogy: delaying obedience to earlier caliphs would be sinful after their imamate was complete.
3
Examine the refutations of sub-objections
The third paragraph addresses the 'withered hand' comment, the conditional bay'ah on killing Uthman's killers, and the claim of coercion. Note how Baqillani counters each: reinterpretation, questioning authenticity, and citing counter-narratives.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the argument continues in the following section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : أفليس قد رُوي أن علياً حضر المسجد ثاني هذا اليوم غَدْوَةً فاجتمع أهل المدينة إليه وأحْضِرَ طلحة والزبير مكرهين فأخرج أولاً طلحة من بيته وأهل البصرة قد حفـوا بـه وحكيم بن جبلة العبدي يحدوه ثم أخرج الزبير وقد أحْدَقَ به أهل الكوفة وملك الأشتر بالسيف من خلفه ثم يحدوه بالسيف من خلفه حدواً حتى أُحْضِرَ المسجد ؛ وخطب على خطبته المشهورة ووصف دخوله في هذا الأمر وقيل لطلحة : بايع! فبايع مكرهاً وصفق على يد علي بيده الشلاء، فقال قائل من أخريات الناس: «لا إله إلا الله ! أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين يد شلاء، والله لا يتم هذا الأمر» ، وقال الناس : يد شلاء وأمر لا يتم ؛ ثم بايع الزبير على هذه الصفة من الإكراه ورُوي أنهما قالا : بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا»؛ وأن طلحة قال: «بايعته واللج على قفي يعني السيف. وأنهما قالا :البصرة: «بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان» ؛ وأن علياً قال بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق»؛ فكيف لا تكون بيعة القوم على هذا الوجه فاسدة وإمامته باطلة ؟ .
قيل لهم : جميع ما ذكرتموه لا يقدح في صحة إمامته؛ لأن البيعة قد كانت تمت ووجب الانقياد لعليّ بعقد من عقدها له ممن ذكرنا قبل حضور طلحة والزبير ومبايعتهما فلا مُعتبر بالمبايعة بعد تمامها وبالوجه الذي وقعت عليه ممن أوقعها إذ كان فعلهما كالتبع لما تقدم ودخول في طاعة قد وجبت عليهما ولو تأخرا عن الانقياد لإمامته لوجب أن يكونا مأثومين في ذلك كما أنه لو تأخر متأخر عن بيعة أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان لوجب تأثيمه بعد إتمام إمامته وقولهما : بايعناك مكْرَهَيْن قد عورض من النقل بما يدفعه وإن وقعت منهما على سبيل الإكراه لم يضر ذلك بإمامة علي رضوان الله عليه لأنها قد ثبتت قبل بيعتهما .
وقول من قال: «أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين . . . » يريد أول يد من أيدي أهل المسجد التي صفقت على يده في ذلك الوقت ولم يرد أنها أول يد بايعته فلا حجة في هذا القول. ويمكن أن يكون هذا القائل ظن أن يد طلحة أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين ولم يكن حضر البيعة عشاء فلا متعلق لأحد في هذا القول . وأما ما روى من قولهم : بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان»، فإنه مما يبعد أن يكون صحيحاً لأن الاتفاق من عليّ ومنهما اتفاق على خطأ في الدين وذلك ما يجب نفيه عنهم ما أمكن ووُجِدَ إليه السبيل وذلك أن عقد الإمامة
If someone says: Has it not been narrated that Ali attended the mosque on the morning of the second day, and the people of Medina gathered to him, and Talha and al-Zubayr were brought forcibly? First Talha was brought out from his house, with the people of Basra surrounding him and Hakim ibn Jabala al-Abdi driving him, then al-Zubayr was brought out with the people of Kufa encircling him and Malik al-Ashtar behind him with a sword, then they drove him with a sword from behind until he was brought to the mosque. And Ali delivered his famous sermon and described his entry into this matter, and it was said to Talha: Pledge allegiance! So he pledged allegiance unwillingly and clapped his withered hand onto Ali's hand. Then a speaker from among the people said: 'There is no god but Allah! The first hand that struck upon the Commander of the Faithful's hand is a withered hand, and by Allah this matter will not be completed.' And the people said: 'A withered hand and a matter that will not be completed.' Then al-Zubayr pledged allegiance in this same manner of coercion. And it was narrated that they both said: 'Our hands pledged allegiance but our hearts did not pledge allegiance to you,' and that Talha said: 'I pledged allegiance with the sword on my neck.' And that they said in Basra: 'We pledged allegiance to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman,' and that Ali said: 'They pledged allegiance to me in Medina and repudiated me in Iraq.' So how could the pledge of these people not be invalid on this basis, and his imamate be void?
It is said to them: All that you have mentioned does not harm the validity of his imamate. Because the pledge of allegiance had already been completed, and obedience to Ali became obligatory by the contract of those who contracted it for him among those we mentioned before the presence of Talha and al-Zubayr and their pledge. So no consideration is given to the allegiance after its completion, nor to the manner in which it occurred from those who performed it, since their action was like a follow-up to what had preceded and an entry into an obedience that had already become obligatory upon them. And if they had delayed obedience to his imamate, they would have been sinful in that, just as if someone delayed in the pledge of allegiance to Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, he would have been sinful after the completion of their imamate. And their statement 'We pledged allegiance under coercion' has been countered by transmitted reports that refute it. Even if it occurred from them under coercion, that does not harm the imamate of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, because it was established before their pledge.
And the statement of whoever said: 'The first hand that struck upon the hand of the Commander of the Faithful...' means the first hand among the hands of the people of the mosque that struck upon his hand at that time, and he did not mean that it was the first hand to pledge allegiance to him, so there is no proof in this statement. And it is possible that this speaker thought that Talha's hand was the first hand to strike upon the hand of the Commander of the Faithful, and he had not attended the evening pledge, so no one can rely on this statement. As for what was narrated from their saying: 'We pledged allegiance to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman,' that is far from being authentic, because an agreement between Ali and them on an error in religion is what must be negated from them as much as possible and as long as a way to do so exists. And that is because the contract of imamate...
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The objector presents multiple narrations that Talha and al-Zubayr were forced to pledge allegiance to Ali, implying that the bay'ah was invalid and thus Ali's caliphate is illegitimate. The answer begins by asserting that the bay'ah had already been completed by other prominent Companions before Talha and al-Zubayr participated, so their later coerced pledge neither adds to nor detracts from Ali's legitimate imamate. The author then addresses each narrated objection: (1) The statement 'the first hand... is a withered hand' is misinterpreted—it refers only to the first hand at that gathering, not the first ever; (2) the claim that they pledged on condition of killing Uthman's killers is improbable because it would imply agreement on a sin; (3) the claim of coercion is met with counter-narrations that refute it, and even if true, the imamate was already established. The author uses analogical reasoning: just as delaying allegiance to earlier caliphs would be sinful after their imamate was complete, so too Talha and al-Zubayr were obligated to obey Ali after the initial valid bay'ah. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'because the contract of imamate...' indicating a further point that would be continued.

إمامة
إكراه
طلحة
الزبير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If some companions were coerced into giving bay'ah, then the caliphate is invalid.
Correction: The imamate is established by a valid bay'ah from qualified individuals; later coercion of others does not void it.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the alleged coercion of Talha and al-Zubayr not invalidate Ali's imamate?
A) Because they later retracted their statements
B) Because the bay'ah was already complete and valid before their pledge
C) Because Ali was not actually the rightful caliph
D) Because Talha and al-Zubayr were not qualified to give bay'ah

Key Takeaway
Ali's caliphate is valid because the initial bay'ah by key Companions established his imamate; subsequent coercion of others does not affect that established authority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever obeyed a legitimate authority (a parent, teacher, or religious leader) reluctantly, using outward compliance as an excuse to withhold true commitment? How does this passage challenge you to examine whether your heart aligns with your actions, even when it is difficult?
?
The objectors argued that external pressure invalidates allegiance. In your own life, where have you allowed circumstances, pressure, or later excuses to weaken your conviction about a truth you once affirmed? What would it mean for you to recommit to that initial acceptance, regardless of what has happened since?
?
Baqillani insists that the initial valid bay'ah established the imamate, making later events irrelevant to its legitimacy. When have you let later doubts or the imperfections of others shake your loyalty to a truth or a leader you once sincerely followed? What step will you take today to renew that loyalty without letting secondary issues undermine it?
