Coercion and the 'First Hand' Objection Answered
Baqillani answers objections about coercion and the 'first hand' saying regarding Ali's bay'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes objections against the validity of Ali's caliphate based on claims of coercion and a misinterpreted saying.

Core Idea
Coercion and later pledges do not invalidate an already-established imamate.

This passage presents an attack on the legitimacy of Ali's imamate, alleging that his bay'ah was obtained through coercion and that a prophetic saying predicted its failure. Imam al-Baqillani responds with a careful chronological and argumentative analysis: the bay'ah was already completed by other companions before Talha and al-Zubayr arrived, so their later coerced pledge is irrelevant. He also reinterprets the 'first hand' saying to remove its sting.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the three claims: coercion, the 'first hand' saying, and the conditional pledge in Basra. Then read the translation.
Notice how the objector presents multiple evidences.
2
Understand Baqillani's first response
Identify the key argument: the bay'ah was already completed before Talha and al-Zubayr pledged, so their later action does not affect validity.
He mentions prior companions who contracted the bay'ah.
3
Understand the second response
Even if coercion occurred, the imamate was already established before their pledge, so it does not harm it.
He analogizes to delaying the pledge of Abu Bakr, etc.
4
Understand the reinterpretation of the saying
Baqillani explains that 'first hand' means the first among those present in the mosque, not the first ever. He also suggests the speaker may have been mistaken.
This defuses the supposed prophecy of failure.
5
Reflect on the method
Notice how Baqillani uses chronological priority and redefinition to refute objections without denying the factual claims.
This is a common kalam technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين يد شلاء، والله لا يتم هذا الأمر، وقال الناس : يد شلاء وأمر لا يتم ; ثم بايع الزبير على هذه الصفة من الإكراه ورُوي أنهما قالا : بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا; وأن طلحة قال: «بايعته واللج على قفي يعني السيف. وأنهما قالا :بالبصرة: «بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان»; وأن علياً قال بايعاني بالمدينة وخلعاني بالعراق; فكيف لا تكون بيعة القوم على هذا الوجه فاسدة وإمامته باطلة ؟ . قيل لهم : جميع ما ذكرتموه لا يقدح في صحة إمامته; لأن البيعة قد كانت تمت ووجب الانقياد لعليّ بعقد من عقدها له ممن ذكرنا قبل حضور طلحة والزبير ومبايعتهما فلا مُعتبر بالمبايعة بعد تمامها وبالوجه الذي وقعت عليه ممن أوقعها إذ كان فعلهما كالتبع لما تقدم ودخول في طاعة قد وجبت عليهما ولو تأخرا عن الانقياد لإمامته لوجب أن يكونا مأثومين في ذلك كما أنه لو تأخر متأخر عن بيعة أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان لوجب تأثيمه بعد إتمام إمامته وقولهما : بايعناك مكْرَهَيْن قد عورض من النقل بما يدفعه وإن وقعت منهما على سبيل الإكراه لم يضر ذلك بإمامة علي رضوان الله عليه لأنها قد ثبتت قبل بيعتهما . وقول من . قال: «أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين . . . » يريد أول يد من أيدي أهل المسجد التي صفقت على يده في ذلك الوقت ولم يرد أنها أول يد بايعته فلا حجة في هذا القول. ويمكن أن يكون هذا القائل ظن أن يد طلحة أول يد صفقت على يد أمير المؤمنين ولم يكن حضر البيعة عشاء فلا متعلق لأحد في هذا القول .
The first hand that shook the hand of the Commander of the Faithful is a crippled hand, and by Allah this matter will not be completed. And the people said: A crippled hand and a matter that is not completed. Then al-Zubayr pledged allegiance on this description of coercion, and it was narrated that they both said: 'Our hands pledged to him but our hearts did not pledge to him.' And that Talha said: 'I pledged to him while the sword was on my neck,' meaning the sword. And that they both said in Basra: 'We pledged to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman.' And that Ali said: 'They pledged to me in Medina and withdrew allegiance from me in Iraq.' So how could the pledge of the people in this manner not be invalid and his imamate false? It was said to them: All that you have mentioned does not detract from the validity of his imamate, because the pledge was already completed and obedience to Ali became obligatory by the contract of those who contracted it for him from among those we mentioned before the presence of Talha and al-Zubayr and their pledge. So no consideration is given to the pledge after its completion and to the manner in which it occurred from those who made it, since their action was like a follow-up to what preceded and an entry into an obedience that had already become obligatory upon them. And if they had delayed in submitting to his imamate, they would have been sinful in that, just as if someone had delayed from the pledge of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, he would have been sinful after the completion of his imamate. And their saying 'We pledged to you coerced' has been countered by transmission that repels it; and even if it occurred from them by way of coercion, that does not harm the imamate of Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, because it was established before their pledge. And the saying of whoever said: 'The first hand that shook the hand of the Commander of the Faithful...' means the first hand from among the hands of the people of the mosque that shook his hand at that time, and it does not mean that it was the first hand that pledged to him, so there is no proof in this saying. And it is possible that this speaker thought that the hand of Talha was the first hand that shook the hand of the Commander of the Faithful, and he had not attended the evening pledge, so there is no basis for anyone in this saying.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector claims that Ali's bay'ah (pledge of allegiance) was invalid due to coercion and the saying 'first hand is crippled.' Baqillani responds first by establishing that the bay'ah was already completed by others before Talha and al-Zubayr arrived; their later pledge is merely a follow-up and does not affect validity. He then addresses the claim of coercion by noting that even if coerced, the imamate had already been settled before their pledge. Finally, he reinterprets the 'first hand' saying: it refers to the first among the people of the mosque present at that time, not the absolute first pledge. Thus, the objections do not undermine Ali's imamate.

Key Terms
بيعة (bay'ah)
إكراه (ikrah)
إمامة (imamah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The 'first hand' saying is sometimes misunderstood as meaning the first pledge ever, foretelling failure.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies it refers to the first among those present at that specific gathering, not the absolute first pledge.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why does the claim of coercion by Talha and al-Zubayr not invalidate Ali's imamate?
A) Because they did not actually say they were coerced.
B) Because the imamate had already been established before their pledge.
C) Because coercion makes a pledge invalid but not the imamate.
D) Because the pledge was not required from them at all.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends Ali's imamate by arguing that the bay'ah was already completed before any alleged coercion, making later claims irrelevant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have firmly committed to a truth—whether in creed, practice, or a decision—do you allow later doubts, objections, or pressures from others to shake that commitment, even when those objections come after the matter was already settled on solid evidence? What would it take for you to stand firm like the early companions who had already completed the bay'ah before Talha and al-Zubayr arrived?
?
The objectors used a single ambiguous saying ('first hand crippled') to cast doubt on Ali's imamate. Are there sayings or hadiths you have heard that you use to justify a position without examining their context or how they relate to the larger body of evidence? Will you commit today to always check the context and established principles before letting such sayings influence your beliefs?
?
Baqillani refuted objections by showing that the imamate was established before the alleged problems occurred. In your own life, do you sometimes let later events or criticisms overshadow a foundation that was already correctly laid? How can you remind yourself that a valid foundation remains valid even when challenges arise later?

The Invalidity of the Condition to Kill Uthman's Murderers
Baqillani refutes the condition to kill Uthman's murderers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the alleged condition to kill Uthman's murderers is invalid according to Baqillani, and why it does not affect the validity of Ali's imamate.

Core Idea
A condition that forces an imam to a specific legal ruling is invalid.

In this passage, Baqillani examines a historical claim about the pledge of allegiance to Ali. He argues that even if the claim were true, the condition attached would be invalid because it contradicts the imam's right to exercise ijtihad. Moreover, procedural and political considerations make such a demand impractical. Most importantly, the earlier contract of imamate takes precedence over any later conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp Baqillani's argument.
Notice the dense reasoning style; Baqillani builds his case methodically.
2
Identify the core argument about ijtihad
Find where Baqillani says the imam is bound by his own ijtihad, not by conditions that impose a specific legal opinion.
This is the key doctrinal point: imamate cannot be contracted with restrictions on ijtihad.
3
Understand the procedural and political conditions
Baqillani lists requirements for executing qisas and explains why delay may be preferable to avoid greater fitna.
These practical considerations show the complexity of implementing such a condition.
4
See the conclusion about imamate's validity
Even if the condition were accepted, the earlier contract of imamate overrides it, and the imam's error does not constitute fisq.
This safeguards the legitimacy of Ali's caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما روى من قولهم : بايعناك على أن تقتل قتلة عثمان، فإنه مما يبعد أن يكون صحيحاً لأن الاتفاق من عليّ ومنهما اتفاق على خطأ في الدين وذلك ما يجب نفيه عنهم ما أمكن ووُجِدَ إليه السبيل وذلك أن عقد الإمامة لرجل على أن يقتل الجماعة بالواحد لا محالة خطأ لا يجوز لأنه متعبد في ذلك باجتهاده والعمل على رأيه وقد يؤدي الإمام اجتهاده إلى أن لا يقتل الجماعة بالواحد وذلك رأى كثير من الفقهاء ; وقد يكون ممن يرى ذلك ثم عنه إلى اجتهاد ثان; فعقد الأمر له على ألا يقيم الحد إلا على مذهب يرجع من مذاهب المسلمين مخصوص فاسد باطل ممن عقده ورضي بـه وليس أن يُنْسَبَ إلى عليّ وطلحة والزبير خطاً مقطوع بفساده يجوز مقطوع بفساده من جهة أخبار الأحاد التي لا يجب العلم بصحتها وعلى أنه إذا ثبت أن علياً ممن يرى قتل الجماعة بالواحد لم يجز أن يقتل جميع قتلة عثمان إلا بأن تقوم البينة على القتلة بأعيانهم وبأن يحضر أولياء الدم مَجْلِسَه ويطالبوا بدم أبيهم ووليهم ولا يكونوا في حكم من يعتقد أنهم بغاة عليه وممن لا يجب استخراج حق لهم دون أن يدخلوا في الطاعة ويرجعوا عن البغي وبأن يُؤدِّي الإمام اجتهاده إلى أن قتل قتلة عثمان لا يؤدي إلى هرج عظيم وفساد شديد قد يكون فيه مثل قتل عثمان أو أعظم منه وإن تأخير إقامة الحد إلى وقت إمكانه وتقصي الحق فيه أولى وأصلح للأمة وألم لشعثهم وأنفى للفساد والتهمة عنهم . هذه أمور كلها تلزم الإمام في إقامة الحدود واستخراج الحقوق وليس لأحد أن يعقد الإمامة لرجل من المسلمين بشريطة تعجيل إقامة حد من حدود الله والعمل فيه برأي الرعية ولا للمعقود له أن يدخل في الإمامة بهذا الشرط فوجب اطراح هذه الرواية لو صحت ولو كانا قد بايعا على هذه الشريطة فقبل هو ذلك لكان هذا خطأ منهم غير أنه لم يكن بقادح في صحة إمامته لأن العقد له قد تقدم هذا العقد الثاني وهذه الشريطة لا معتبر بها لأن الغلط في هذا من الإمام الثابتة إمامته ليس بفسق يوجب خَلْعَه وسقوط فرض طاعته عنـد أحد .
As for what was narrated of their saying: 'We pledged to you on condition that you kill the murderers of Uthman,' this is unlikely to be sound because the agreement between Ali and them would be an agreement upon an error in religion, and that is something that must be negated of them as much as possible and as far as there is a way to it. This is because the contract of imamate for a man on condition that he kill a group for one is necessarily an error that is not permissible, for he is bound in that matter by his own ijtihad (juristic reasoning) and acting on his opinion. The imam's ijtihad may lead him not to kill a group for one, and that is the opinion of many jurists. And it may be that he holds that opinion, then he turns from it to another ijtihad. So contracting authority for him on condition that he only establish the prescribed punishment (hadd) according to a particular school among the schools of Muslims is corrupt and invalid in those who contract it and are pleased with it. And it is not to be attributed to Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr a definite error which is definitely invalid from the reports of single narrations (akhbar al-ahad) whose soundness is not necessarily known. And if it is established that Ali is among those who hold the opinion of killing a group for one, it is not permissible for him to kill all the murderers of Uthman unless evidence is established against the murderers individually, and the legal guardians of the blood attend his court and demand the blood of their father and guardian, and they are not in the position of those who are considered rebels (bughah) against him and from whom it is not obligatory to extract a right unless they enter into obedience and desist from rebellion; and unless the imam's ijtihad leads him to the conclusion that killing the murderers of Uthman does not lead to great turmoil and severe corruption in which there might be something like the killing of Uthman or greater, and that delaying the establishment of the prescribed punishment until it is possible and fully investigating the right in it is more appropriate and better for the community, more healing for their disunity, and more repelling of corruption and suspicion from them. These are all matters that are incumbent upon the imam in the establishment of the prescribed punishments and the extraction of rights. It is not for anyone to contract the imamate for a man from the Muslims with the condition of hastening the establishment of a prescribed punishment of Allah and acting in it according to the opinion of the subjects, nor is it for the one for whom it is contracted to enter into the imamate with this condition. So it is necessary to discard this narration even if it were sound. And if they had pledged to him on this condition and he accepted it, that would have been an error on their part, but it would not have been a detraction from the validity of his imamate, because the first contract for him had preceded this second contract, and this condition is not to be considered, because the error in this from the imam whose imamate is established is not a sinfulness (fisq) that necessitates his removal (khal') and the fall of the obligation of obedience to him according to anyone.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation (objection-and-answer). The objector claims that Talha and al-Zubayr pledged to Ali on condition that he kill the murderers of Uthman. Baqillani argues this is unlikely because it implies an agreement on an error in religion: the imamate cannot be conditioned to execute a hadd according to a specific opinion, as the imam must follow his own ijtihad. He explains that killing a group for one is not universally accepted, and even if Ali held that view, procedural conditions (witnesses, presence of guardians, etc.) must be met. Moreover, delaying punishment may be better to avoid greater fitna. Finally, even if the condition was made and accepted, the earlier contract of imamate supersedes it, so Ali's imamate remains valid.

Key Terms
شرط (shart)
اجتهاد (ijtihad)
حد (hadd)
فسق (fisq)
خلع (khal')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that a condition in a pledge automatically invalidates the imamate.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the first valid contract overrides later conditions, and the imam's error does not constitute fisq.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why would the condition to kill Uthman's murderers be invalid?
A) Because Ali was unwilling to kill anyone.
B) Because it imposes a specific legal opinion on the imam, which contradicts his right to ijtihad.
C) Because Talha and al-Zubayr had no right to make conditions.
D) Because the murderers were already killed.

Key Takeaway
An imam cannot be bound by conditions that restrict his ijtihad, and a later condition does not nullify an earlier valid contract of imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you demand something from a leader or someone in authority, do you respect their right to exercise their own judgment based on circumstances, or do you insist on your own condition? How does Baqillani's argument challenge your tendency to impose conditions?
?
Baqillani argues that delaying justice may be better for the community if immediate action causes greater harm. Think of a situation in your own life where you insisted on immediate justice or punishment despite knowing it might worsen the conflict. Would you now delay it for the sake of harmony?
?
The first contract of imamate overrides later conditions. Reflect on a primary commitment in your life—such as your pledge to Allah or a promise to your family. Have you allowed later demands or conditions to weaken that commitment? What would it take for you to reaffirm that initial pledge?

War and Withdrawal Do Not Invalidate Imamate
Baqillani responds to an objection about war and withdrawal affecting Ali's imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that once an imamate is confirmed, neither war nor withdrawal of allegiance by prominent figures can invalidate it.

Core Idea
Confirmed imamate cannot be undone by rebellion.

After establishing the correct imam, Baqillani addresses a potential objection: what about the actions of Talha and al-Zubayr against Ali? Did their war and possible withdrawal of allegiance affect Ali's imamate? In this passage, he delivers a sharp response, asserting that such actions have no impact on the validity of a confirmed imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection raised against Baqillani's position: the questioner asks about the war and possible khul' by two prominent companions.
Notice the phrasing: 'If it is said...' introduces a hypothetical opponent.
2
Examine Baqillani's response
Read Baqillani's answer: he dismisses the withdrawal as 'nothing' and emphasizes that it does not detract from the validity of the imamate.
Key phrase: 'because his imamate has been confirmed; so it does not become invalid after its confirmation.'
3
Grasp the underlying principle
Understand the principle: the validity of imamate is fixed by the initial contract of allegiance and is not shaken by subsequent opposition, even from important figures.
This principle safeguards the stability of political authority in Sunni thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما تقولون في حربهما له ومطالبتهما بهذا الباب وخلعهما له إن كانا خلعاه؟ قيل له : أما خلعهما له إن صح ، فإنه ليس بشيء ولا قادح في صحة إمامته ولا موجب لسقوط طاعته لأن إمامته قد صحت; فلا ينخلع بعد صحتها بخلعهما له ولا بخلع غيرهما ولا بترك الذهاب إلى بعض

Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks about the war waged by Talha and al-Zubayr against Ali and their possible khul' (withdrawal of allegiance). Baqillani responds that even if the withdrawal is established, it has no effect: the imamate remains valid because it was already confirmed. Withdrawal by some individuals does not undo the obligation of obedience to the established imam. The argument is cut off mid-sentence, but the main point is clear.

Key Terms
حرب (harb)
خلع (khul')
طاعة (ta'ah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rebellion or withdrawal of allegiance by prominent companions invalidates the imamate.
Correction: Baqillani teaches that once the imamate is validly established, it cannot be undone by such actions. The authority of the imam remains binding.

Checkpoint

B) It has no effect because the imamate was already confirmed.
C) It shows that Ali's imamate was originally invalid.
D) It requires a new election for a different caliph.

Key Takeaway
Once an imamate is validly established, it remains binding regardless of opposition or withdrawal of allegiance by individuals.

Refuting the Claim that Ali Executed a Group for One Person
The author refutes the claim that Ali permitted executing a group for one person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani deconstructs the evidential and legal basis of a historical claim about Ali's ruling.

Core Idea
A claim's weakness is exposed through both unreliable evidence and flawed legal reasoning.

This passage from Imam Baqillani tackles a controversial historical claim about Ali's judicial practice. The author systematically dismantles the claim, first by arguing the inherent invalidity of punishing a group for one, then by questioning the reliability of the reports, and finally by outlining the impossible conditions for such a ruling to be implemented. This lesson walks through his multi-layered refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how the author builds his argument from a general principle to specific conditions.
Pay attention to the shift from legal reasoning to hadith criticism.
2
Identify the core thesis
Find where the author declares the claim 'categorically an error'. This is his starting point.
He uses the phrase 'لا محالة خطأ لا يجوز'.
3
Examine the ijtihad argument
The author says the imam is bound by his ijtihad and many jurists disagree with the ruling. Understand why this matters for the claim's validity.
This shows the claim contradicts mainstream juristic opinion.
4
Understand the contract condition critique
The author argues that stipulating a specific madhhab in the imamate contract is corrupt. Reflect on what this implies about the original claim.
This is a legal technicality that undermines the supposed contract with Ali.
5
Analyze the evidential attack
The author states the attribution to Ali is based on ahad reports. Consider the implication: such reports do not yield certain knowledge, so the claim cannot be conclusively proven.
This is a methodological point about the reliability of historical reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لرجل على أن يقتل الجماعة بالواحد لا محالة خطأ لا يجوز لأنه متعبد في ذلك باجتهاده والعمل على رأيه وقد يؤدي الإمام اجتهاده إلى أن لا يقتل الجماعة بالواحد وذلك رأى كثير من الفقهاء ؛ وقد يكون ممن يرى ذلك ثم عنه إلى اجتهاد ثان؛ فعقد الأمر له على ألا يقيم الحد إلا على مذهب يرجع من مذاهب المسلمين مخصوص فاسد باطل ممن عقده ورضي بـه وليس أن يُنْسَبَ إلى عليّ وطلحة والزبير خطاً مقطوع بفساده يجوز مقطوع بفساده من جهة أخبار الأحاد التي لا يجب العلم بصحتها وعلى أنه إذا ثبت أن علياً ممن يرى قتل الجماعة بالواحد لم يجز أن يقتل جميع قتلة عثمان إلا بأن تقوم البينة على القتلة بأعيانهم وبأن يحضر أولياء الدم مَجْلِسَه ويطالبوا بدم أبيهم ووليهم ولا يكونوا في حكم من يعتقد أنهم بغاة عليه وممن لا يجب استخراج حق لهم دون أن يدخلوا في الطاعة ويرجعوا عن البغي وبأن يُؤدِّي الإمام اجتهاده إلى أن قتل قتلة عثمان لا يؤدي إلى هرج عظيم وفساد شديد قد يكون فيه مثل قتل عثمان أو أعظم منه وإن تأخير إقامة الحد إلى وقت إمكانه وتقصي الحق فيه أولى وأصلح للأمة وألم لشعثهم وأنفى للفساد والتهمة عنهم .
It is not permitted for a man to kill a group for one individual; it is categorically an error, not permissible, because he is bound in that by his ijtihad and acting on his opinion. The imam's ijtihad may lead him to not kill a group for one individual, and that is the opinion of many jurists. And he may be among those who hold that view, then he may change to a second ijtihad. So making the contract for him on condition that he only establish the prescribed punishment according to a madhhab derived from the madhahib of the Muslims—specifically—is corrupt and invalid from the one who made the contract and consented to it. And it is not to be attributed to Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr as a clear error conclusively invalid, as a conclusive invalidity from the perspective of ahad reports which certain knowledge of their authenticity is not required. And that if it is established that Ali was among those who hold the view of killing a group for one individual, it would not be permissible to kill all the killers of Uthman unless the evidence is established against the killers individually, and the guardians of the blood present themselves in his assembly and demand the blood of their father and their patron, and they are not considered as rebels against him and among those for whom it is not obligatory to extract their rights without their entering into obedience and desisting from rebellion; and unless the imam's ijtihad leads to that killing the killers of Uthman does not lead to great turmoil and severe corruption that may involve something like the killing of Uthman or greater; and that delaying the establishment of the prescribed punishment until its possible time and pursuing the truth in it is better and more beneficial for the community, more healing for their divisions, and more repelling of corruption and suspicion from them.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a claim made about Ali's stance on executing a group for a single murder. The author begins by declaring the claim itself invalid: it is not permissible to kill a group for one person, as the ruler is obligated to follow his own ijtihad, and many jurists hold this view. The author then criticizes the idea of stipulating a particular legal opinion in the imamate contract as corrupt and invalid. He then addresses the attribution of the opposite view to Ali, Talha, and al-Zubayr, stating that it is an error based on unreliable ahad reports, which do not yield certain knowledge. Even if the report were accepted, the author argues that the conditions for executing all killers of Uthman would not be met: individual guilt must be proven, the blood guardians must come forward and demand justice while not being considered rebels, and the imam must be certain that executing the killers will not lead to greater fitna. The passage thus systematically undermines the evidential and legal basis of the claim.

Key Terms
خبر واحد
اجتهاد
إمامة
حد
فساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Criticizing a report's reliability is equivalent to denying the event it reports.
Correction: The author critiques the evidential basis of the claim but does not necessarily deny that Ali may have taken some action.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the claim that Ali permitted killing a group for one person invalid?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran
B) Because it is based on ahad reports and the conditions for punishment are not met
C) Because Ali was not present at the time
D) Because Talha and al-Zubayr opposed it

Key Takeaway
The claim that Ali executed a group for one person is unfounded both evidentially and legally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever embraced a negative claim about a Companion or scholar based solely on a report you heard, without checking the reliability of the evidence or the legal reasoning behind it? Will you commit to seeking both sound narration and sound principles before forming opinions about the Salaf?
?
The author shows that even if a report were true, the application may be invalid due to broader consequences. Is there a 'truth' you insist on applying in your life that is causing harm to yourself or others? Will you ask Allah to give you the wisdom to consider both truth and its consequences, as the imam must?
?
When you hear a controversial historical accusation, does your heart lean toward defense or doubt? How does this lesson challenge you to examine both the reliability of the report and the coherence of the accusation with established Islamic principles? Will you from now on refuse to accept any claim without such scrutiny?

Invalidity of Stipulations in the Imamate Contract
The author invalidates stipulations in the imamate contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why conditions placed in the imamate contract are invalid and do not undermine the imam's authority.

Core Idea
Stipulations in the imamate contract are invalid but do not invalidate the imamate.

The author continues his discussion on the imamate by addressing a hypothetical scenario where someone contracts the imamate with a condition about implementing a specific punishment. He argues that such conditions are invalid, and even if accepted, they do not affect the imamate's validity because the original contract precedes them. This passage clarifies the limits of contractual flexibility in the imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the repetition of 'khata' – it highlights the error.
2
Identify the key claim
The author states that it is not permissible to contract the imamate with a condition, and even if done, it does not invalidate the imamate.
3
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning is that the original contract precedes the condition, and the error is not a sin requiring removal.
The author contrasts 'khata' (error) with 'fisq' (sin).
4
Connect to broader context
The author refers to previously mentioned events as the only grounds for removal, showing consistency.
This ties back to earlier lessons on removal criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذه أمور كلها تلزم الإمام في إقامة الحدود واستخراج الحقوق وليس لأحد أن يعقد الإمامة لرجل من المسلمين بشريطة تعجيل إقامة حد من حدود الله والعمل فيه برأي الرعية ولا للمعقود له أن يدخل في الإمامة بهذا الشرط فوجب اطراح هذه الرواية لو صحت ولو كانا قد بايعا على هذه الشريطة فقبل هو ذلك لكان هذا خطأ ذلك لكان هذا خطأ منهم غير أنه لم يكن بقادح في صحة إمامته لأن العقد له قد تقدم هذا العقد الثاني وهذه الشريطة لا معتبر بها لأن الغلط في هذا من الإمام الثابتة إمامته ليس بفسق يوجب خَلْعَه وسقوط فرض طاعته عنــد أحد . مذاهب المسلمين في إقامة الحد؛ إنما ينخلع بالأحداث التي ذكرناها من قبل فقط .
These are all matters that are incumbent upon the imam in establishing prescribed punishments and extracting rights. And it is not for anyone to contract the imamate for a man among the Muslims on the condition of hastening the establishment of a prescribed punishment from God's prescribed punishments and acting in it according to the opinion of the subjects; nor for the one for whom it is contracted to enter into the imamate with this condition. So it is necessary to discard this narration even if it were authentic. And if they had pledged allegiance on this condition and he accepted it, it would be an error on their part—an error on their part—but it would not be a defect in the validity of his imamate, because the contract for him had already preceded this second contract, and this condition is not regarded, because the error in this from the imam whose imamate is established is not a sin that necessitates his removal and the fall of the obligation of obedience to him according to anyone. The madhahib of the Muslims [vary] in establishing the prescribed punishment; he is only removed by the events we mentioned before only.
Source pages p. 555

Commentary
This passage continues the argument about the imamate contract. The author first enumerates the obligations of the imam in establishing punishments and rights. He then states that it is not permissible for anyone to contract the imamate with a condition requiring the imam to hasten a specific punishment according to the subjects' opinion. Even if such a condition were made and accepted, it would be an error but not invalidate the imamate because the original contract precedes the condition, and an error in ijtihad is not a sin requiring removal. The mention of 'the madhahib of the Muslims' points out that different schools exist on punishment, and the imam is only removed for the causes previously mentioned (e.g., apostasy, injustice).

Key Terms
إمامة

شرط
خلع
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any error in judgment by the imam automatically invalidates his imamate.
Correction: The author clarifies that only sins (fisq) necessitate removal, not mere ijtihadi errors.

Checkpoint
What is the author's view on a condition in the imamate contract regarding the establishment of a hadd punishment?
A) It is valid and must be fulfilled
B) It is invalid and makes the contract null
C) It is invalid but does not affect the imamate's validity
D) It is recommended but not binding

Key Takeaway
Stipulations in the imamate contract are invalid and do not affect the imamate's validity; only major sins require removal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at a leader—whether in your community, your workplace, or your family—do you set conditions for your obedience? Have you ever withdrawn your support because of a mistake you considered unforgivable, forgetting that error is not always sin? What would it take for you to examine your own heart and repent of the conditions you place on those in authority over you, and instead commit to obedience within the bounds that Allah has set?
?
The imam's error in accepting a condition is called a 'mistake' not a 'sin' by this text. Can you think of a time you classified someone's mistake as deliberate disobedience, even though it might have been an honest error? How does this lesson challenge you to re-evaluate your judgments of others, especially those in positions of authority? Will you actively train yourself to distinguish between genuine sin and fallibility?
?
This lesson teaches that the imamate contract is not invalidated by a later condition, because the original contract precedes. In your own life, do you honor your primary commitments (like marriage, pledges, promises) even when later conditions appear? Where have you allowed secondary grievances to overshadow the original covenant, and what step will you take today to reaffirm that original commitment?

Objection and Answer on Talha and al-Zubayr
Al-Baqillani answers an objection about Talha and al-Zubayr's actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Baqillani considers the war of Talha and al-Zubayr against Ali as ijtihad rather than rebellion, and why their alleged removal of Ali has no effect.

Core Idea
Armed opposition by qualified scholars is ijtihad, not rebellion.

This passage addresses a sensitive historical issue: the conflict between Ali and some of his prominent contemporaries. The opponent argues that Talha and al-Zubayr's war against Ali and their alleged declaration of his removal (khul') should invalidate his imamate. Al-Baqillani responds by distinguishing between the act of khul' and the war itself, showing that neither undermines Ali's legitimate authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the structure: first the objection, then the answer beginning with 'qila lahu'.
The opponent raises two issues: khul' and war.
2
Understand the argument on khul'
Al-Baqillani states that even if Talha and al-Zubayr attempted to remove Ali, it has no effect because Ali's imamate was already valid. Removal only occurs for specific causes (apostasy, clear injustice) mentioned earlier.
Khul' by individuals cannot undo a valid imamate.
3
Understand the argument on the war
The war was an ijtihadi matter; they were qualified jurists who followed their own reasoning. It was not sinful rebellion but a sincere error of judgment.
Ijtihad errors do not negate the imam's authority.
4
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider the principle that armed opposition by qualified scholars is not necessarily rebellion; it can be ijtihad. This is important for understanding early Islamic history and methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فما تقولون في حربهما له ومطالبتهما بهذا الباب وخلعهما له إن كانا خلعاه؟ قيل له : أما خلعهما له إن صح ، فإنه ليس بشيء ولا قادح في صحة إمامته ولا موجب لسقوط طاعته لأن إمامته قد صحت؛ فلا ينخلع بعد صحتها بخلعهما له ولا بخلع غيرهما ولا بترك الذهاب إلى بعض مذاهب المسلمين في إقامة الحد؛ إنما ينخلع بالأحداث التي ذكرناها من قبل فقط . فأما حربهما له على ذلك فإنه اجتهاد منهما وما أداهما الرأي إليه وهما من أهل الفقه والرأي؛ وكذلك عائشة
If someone says: 'What do you say about their war against him and their demanding this matter and their removal of him if they removed him?' It is said to him: 'As for their removal of him, if it is true, it is nothing and does not detract from the validity of his imamate nor necessitates the fall of obedience to him, because his imamate has been established; so he is not removed after its validity by their removal of him nor by the removal of others nor by abandoning going to some madhahib of the Muslims in establishing the prescribed punishment; he is only removed by the events we mentioned before only. As for their war against him on that, it was ijtihad from them and what their opinion led them to, and they are among the people of jurisprudence and opinion; and likewise Aisha.'
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent asks about Talha and al-Zubayr's war against Ali and their alleged declaration of his removal. The author answers by first addressing the claim of khul' (removal from imamate): even if they attempted it, it has no effect because Ali's imamate was already established and cannot be undone by their action; removal only occurs for the specific causes mentioned earlier (such as apostasy or clear injustice). Then he addresses the war itself: it was an ijtihadi matter; they followed their own reasoning as qualified jurists, and therefore it was an error of ijtihad rather than rebellion. The author includes Aisha in the same category.

Key Terms
خلع
اجتهاد
إمامة
حرب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Armed opposition to a caliph, especially by prominent Companions, automatically invalidates the caliph's authority and makes the opposition sinful rebels.
Correction: Al-Baqillani argues that if the opponents are qualified scholars (mujtahidun), their war can be an error of ijtihad, not rebellion. It does not affect the caliph's legitimacy.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, what is the effect of Talha and al-Zubayr's alleged removal (khul') of Ali?
A) It invalidates Ali's imamate immediately
B) It has no effect because Ali's imamate was already established
C) It requires re-election
D) It is a sign of apostasy

Key Takeaway
The actions of Talha, al-Zubayr, and Aisha are excused as ijtihad and do not undermine Ali's legitimate imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone in authority whose actions you disagree with, do you immediately assume they are wrong or even sinful? How does this lesson's distinction between ijtihad and sin challenge your impulse to judge? What would it take for you to extend the same charity to those you oppose as al-Baqillani extends to Talha and al-Zubayr?
?
Imagine you are convinced that a leader has made a grave mistake. How do you know whether your opposition is a sincere ijtihad or a cover for personal grievance? This lesson shows that even the greatest companions could err in their ijtihad. What does that mean for your own confidence in your judgments? Are you willing to humbly admit that you might be wrong?
?
This lesson argues that an imam's removal is only for specific causes, not by popular declaration. Are there people in your life—parents, teachers, leaders—whose authority you have mentally 'removed' because they didn't meet your expectations? How does al-Baqillani's reasoning call you to repentance and renewed obedience? What concrete step can you take today to restore that respect?

Scholarly Positions on the Battle of the Camel
Baqillani classifies four scholarly views on the Battle of the Camel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main scholarly positions regarding the conflict between Ali and his opponents at the Battle of the Camel.

Core Idea
Scholars disagreed on the Battle of the Camel, viewing it as ijtihad, error, or repentance.

This passage by Imam Baqillani presents a map of the different scholarly stances on the conflict between Ali and his opponents. Instead of a single verdict, the tradition contains a spectrum ranging from treating it as a valid ijtihad to affirming repentance. Understanding these positions is key to grasping how classical Sunni scholars navigated historical disputes among Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview of the different positions. Notice the enumeration markers 'among them are those who...'.
The passage lists four main views plus a fifth from the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify each position
Go through the passage and list each distinct view: (1) ijtihad where every mujtahid is correct, (2) truth is one with Ali, opponents err without sin, (3) certainty of Ali's correctness and forgiveness for opponents, (4) those who repented with evidence, (5) Mu'tazila suspending judgment.
Each view is introduced by 'منهم من'.
3
Examine the evidence for repentance
Look at the narrations cited: al-Zubayr's return, Aisha's regret and weeping, Talha's pledge to Ali at death. Also the Prophetic hadith about ten Quraysh in Paradise including Talha and al-Zubayr.
This evidence supports the view that the opponents repented.
4
Reflect on the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila are mentioned as pausing (tawaqquf) regarding all parties. Consider why they might refrain from judgment.
Tawaqquf reflects caution in evaluating figures of early Islamic history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن الناس من يجعل هذه المسألة من مسائل الاجتهاد ويقول : إن كل مجتهد مصيب كإصابتهم في سائر مسائل الأحكام ومنهم من يقول إن الحق منها في واحد، وهو رأي علي وقوله وإن مخالفه مخطىء في الاجتهاد خطاً لا يبلغ به الإثم والفسوق بل الإثم عنه موضوع ومنهم من يقطع بصواب أمير المؤمنين وخطأ من خالفه ونازعه وأنه مغفور له ومنهم من يقول : إنهم تابوا من ذلك ويستدل برجوع الزبير وندم عائشة إذا ذكروا لها يوم الجمل وبكائها حتى تبل خِمَارَها وقولها : وددت أن لو كان لي عشرون ولداً من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلّم كلهم مثل عبد الرحمن بن الحارث بن هشام، وأني تكلتهم، ولم يكن ما كان مني يوم الجمل، وقولها: لقد أحدقت بي يوم الجمل الاسينة حتى صرت على البعير مثل اللُّجة. وأن طلحة قال لشاب من عسكر علي، وهو يجود بنفسه : أمدد يدك أبايعك لأمير المؤمنين، وما هذا نحوه . والمعتمد عندهم في ذلك قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : عشرة من قريش في الجنة وعد فيهم طلحة والزبير قالوا: ولم يكن ليخبر بذلك إلا علم منه بأنهما سيتوبان مما أحدثاه ويوافيان بالندم والإقلاع . وعن أئمة المعتزلة من يقف في عليّ وطلحة والزبير وعائشة ولا يدري
Among the people are those who make this issue one of ijtihad and say: 'Every mujtahid is correct, just as they are correct in other legal issues.' Among them are those who say that the truth in it is one, and that is the opinion of Ali and his statement, and that whoever opposes him is mistaken in ijtihad, an error that does not reach the level of sin and wickedness; rather, the sin is set aside from him. Among them are those who are certain of the correctness of the Commander of the Faithful and the error of those who opposed and disputed him, and that it is forgiven for him. Among them are those who say that they repented from that, and they deduce by the return of al-Zubayr and the regret of Aisha when the Battle of the Camel was mentioned to her, and her crying until she soaked her veil, and her saying: 'I wish I had twenty sons from the Messenger of God, all like Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith ibn Hisham, and that I had lost them, and that what happened from me on the day of the Camel had not happened,' and her saying: 'On the day of the Camel, the spears surrounded me until I became on the camel like a wave.' And that Talha said to a young man from Ali's army, while he was giving up his soul: 'Extend your hand, I pledge allegiance to you for the Commander of the Faithful,' and other similar reports. And what is relied upon among them in that is the saying of the Prophet: 'Ten of Quraysh are in Paradise,' and he counted among them Talha and al-Zubayr. They said: 'He would not have informed of that except with knowledge that both of them would repent from what they committed and would come with regret and desistance.' And from the leaders of the Mu'tazila are those who pause regarding Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Aisha and do not know.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a classification of scholarly positions regarding the conflict between Ali and his opponents at the Battle of the Camel. The author lists four main views: (1) Some consider it a matter of ijtihad where both sides are correct, as in other legal rulings. (2) Some hold that the truth is with Ali alone, and his opponents erred in ijtihad—an error that does not make them sinful. (3) Some are certain that Ali was correct and his opponents were wrong, but they are forgiven. (4) Some claim that they repented, citing evidence such as al-Zubayr's return, Aisha's regret and weeping, and Talha's pledge to Ali at death. The author notes that the proof of the Prophet's statement about ten Quraysh in Paradise supports their repentance. Finally, the Mu'tazila are mentioned as taking a position of tawaqquf (suspending judgment) without taking sides.

Key Terms
اجتهاد
مصيب
خطأ
توبة
وقف
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All scholars considered Ali's opponents sinful.
Correction: The passage shows many viewed it as ijtihad or forgivable error, and some even affirmed their repentance.

Checkpoint
What is the position of those who say 'every mujtahid is correct' regarding the conflict?
A) They condemn both sides
B) They consider both sides correct in their ijtihad
C) They only consider Ali correct
D) They suspend judgment

Key Takeaway
Scholars offered multiple valid interpretations of the conflict, from ijtihad to repentance, reflecting the complexity of evaluating historical events among the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a conflict between two people you respect, do you automatically choose a side, or do you consider that both may have valid perspectives? How can you apply Baqillani's classification to withhold judgment and seek a balanced view?
?
The passage shows that even the Companions who opposed Ali were later believed to have repented with deep regret. Is there an area in your life where you need to sincerely repent and show regret, even if others think you were justified?
?
The Mu'tazila 'pause' (tawaqquf) reflects humility in not passing judgment on matters beyond one's knowledge. Where in your daily interactions do you need to pause and refrain from judging others, especially when you lack full understanding of their situation?

Differing Views on the Battle of the Camel
Baqillani enumerates the differing Muslim views on the Battle of the Camel and gives his preferred explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four main Muslim views on the actions of the Companions in the Battle of the Camel, including the Mu'tazila position, and Baqillani's own preferred explanation.

Core Idea
The Companions' actions in the battle are interpreted through ijtihad, repentance, and forgiveness, not sin.

In this passage, Baqillani presents a spectrum of Muslim opinions on the Battle of the Camel, showing how classical theologians approached the historical conflict among the Companions. He lists four major views, notes the Mu'tazila's suspension of judgment, and then gives his own view that the battle was the result of a conspiracy by the killers of Uthman. This lesson will help you appreciate the nuanced approach to evaluating the actions of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how Baqillani begins by setting the context of ijtihad.
2
Identify the four views
Find the four distinct positions Baqillani lists: (1) both sides correct by ijtihad, (2) truth with Ali alone but opponents not sinful, (3) Ali correct and opponents forgiven, (4) they repented.
3
Examine the evidence for repentance
Notice the hadith about ten Quraysh in Paradise and the stories of Aisha's regret and Talhah's pledge as evidence for the repentance view.
4
See the Mu'tazila position
Baqillani mentions that some Mu'tazila imams paused judgment, not knowing who was correct.
5
Understand Baqillani's preferred view
Baqillani endorses the view that the battle was a sudden conspiracy by Uthman's killers, making each side defensive and thus correct.
This is the view he calls 'correct and well-known'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذاهب المسلمين في إقامة الحد؛ إنما ينخلع بالأحداث التي ذكرناها من قبل فقط. فأما حربهما له على ذلك فإنه اجتهاد منهما وما أداهما الرأي إليه وهما من أهل الفقه والرأي؛ وكذلك عائشة. فمن الناس من يجعل هذه المسألة من مسائل الاجتهاد ويقول: إن كل مجتهد مصيب كإصابتهم في سائر مسائل الأحكام. ومنهم من يقول إن الحق منها في واحد، وهو رأي علي وقوله وإن مخالفه مخطىء في الاجتهاد خطأ لا يبلغ به الإثم والفسوق بل الإثم عنه موضوع. ومنهم من يقطع بصواب أمير المؤمنين وخطأ من خالفه ونازعه وأنه مغفور له. ومنهم من يقول: إنهم تابوا من ذلك ويستدل برجوع الزبير وندم عائشة إذا ذكروا لها يوم الجمل وبكائها حتى تبل خمارها وقولها: وددت أن لو كان لي عشرون ولداً من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كلهم مثل عبد الرحمن بن الحارث بن هشام، وأني تكلتهم، ولم يكن ما كان مني يوم الجمل، وقولها: لقد أحدقت بي يوم الجمل الأسنّة حتى صرت على البعير مثل اللجة. وأن طلحة قال لشاب من عسكر علي، وهو يجود بنفسه: أمدد يدك أبايعك لأمير المؤمنين، وما هذا نحوه. والمعتمد عندهم في ذلك قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: عشرة من قريش في الجنة وعد فيهم طلحة والزبير. قالوا: ولم يكن ليخبر بذلك إلا علم منه بأنهما سيتوبان مما أحدثاه ويوافيان بالندم والإقلاع. ومن أئمة المعتزلة من يقف في علي وطلحة والزبير وعائشة ولا يدري من المصيب منهم ومن المخطىء كعمرو بن عبيد وواصل بن عطاء من مال إلى قولهم. وقال جلّة من أهل العلم إن الوقعة بالبصرة بينهم كانت على غير عزيمة على الحرب بل فجاءة وكان على سبيل دفع كل واحد من الفريقين عن أنفسهم لظنه أن الفريق الآخر قد غدر بها لأن الأمر قد كان انتظم بينهم وتم الصلح والتفرق على الرضا فخاف قتلة عثمان من التمكن منهم والإحاطة بهم فاجتمعوا وتشاوروا واختلفوا ثم اتفقت آراؤهم على أن يفترقوا فرقتين ويبدؤوا بالحرب سحرة في العسكرين ويختلطوا ويصيح الفريق الذي في عسكر علي: غدر طلحة والزبير ويصيح الفريق الآخر الذي في عسكر طلحة والزبير: غدر علي! فتم لهم ذلك على ما دبروه ونشبت الحرب؛ فكان كل فريق منهم دافعا لمكروه عن نفسه ومانعاً من الإشاطة بدمه. وهذا صواب من الفريقين وطاعة الله تعالى، إذا وقع القتال والامتناع منهم على هذه السبيل. فهذا هو الصحيح المشهور وإليه نميل وبه نقول. فإن قال قائل: فإذا كانت إمامة علي من الصحة والثبوت بحيث وصفتم فما تقولون في تأخر سعد بن أبي وقاص وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن نفيل بن عمر ومحمد بن مسلمة وأسامة بن زيد وسلامة بن وقش وغير هؤلاء ممن يكثر عددهم وقعودهم عن نصرته والدخول في طاعته؟ قيل لهم: ليس في جميع القاعدين ممن أسميناه أو أضربنا عن ذكره من طعن في إمامته واعتقد فسادها وإنما قعدوا عن نصرته على حرب المسلمين لتخوفهم من ذلك.
The positions of Muslims regarding the establishment of the limit: it is only removed by the events we mentioned before. As for their fighting him for that, it was their ijtihad and what their opinion led them to, and they are people of jurisprudence and opinion; and likewise Aisha. Among the people, some make this issue one of ijtihad and say: every mujtahid is correct, like their correctness in all other legal issues. And among them are those who say that the truth lies in one of them, and it is the opinion and statement of Ali, and that whoever opposes him is mistaken in ijtihad, a mistake that does not reach the level of sin and disobedience, rather sin is waived from him. And among them are those who decide the correctness of the Commander of the Faithful and the error of those who opposed and contested him, and that it is forgiven for him. And among them are those who say that they repented from that, and they adduce the return of al-Zubayr and the regret of Aisha when they reminded her of the Day of the Camel and her weeping until her veil became wet, and her saying: 'I wish I had twenty sons from the Messenger of Allah, all of them like Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith ibn Hisham, and that I had lost them, and that what happened to me on the Day of the Camel had not happened,' and her saying: 'The spears surrounded me on the Day of the Camel until I became on the camel like a wave.' And that Talhah said to a youth in Ali's army, while he was dying: 'Extend your hand so that I pledge allegiance to you for the Commander of the Faithful,' and similar things. And the relied-upon among them regarding that is the saying of the Prophet: 'Ten from Quraysh are in Paradise,' including Talhah and al-Zubayr. They said: He would not have informed of that except out of knowledge that they would repent from what they had done and come with regret and desistance. And among the imams of the Mu'tazila are those who pause regarding Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr, and Aisha, and do not know who is correct among them and who is mistaken, like Amr ibn Ubayd and Wasil ibn Ata who inclined to their statement. And a group of scholars said that the incident at Basra between them was not based on a determination to fight, but rather it was sudden, and it was on the basis of each of the two parties defending themselves, thinking that the other party had betrayed them because the matter had been arranged among them, the peace was concluded, and they separated with satisfaction. Then the killers of Uthman feared being captured and surrounded, so they gathered and consulted and differed, then their opinions agreed to split into two groups and start the war at dawn in the two camps, mix together, and the group in Ali's camp would shout: 'Talhah and al-Zubayr have betrayed!' and the other group in the camp of Talhah and al-Zubayr would shout: 'Ali has betrayed!' So they accomplished that as they planned, and the war broke out; thus each party was repelling harm from itself and preventing the shedding of its blood. And this is correct from both parties and obedience to Allah, if the fighting and abstention occurred in this manner. This is the correct and well-known view, and we incline to it and we say it. If someone says: Since the imamate of Ali is valid and established as you described, what do you say about the delay of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd ibn Amr ibn Nufayl, Muhammad ibn Maslamah, Usamah ibn Zayd, Salamah ibn Waqsh, and others of those who are numerous, and their sitting back from supporting him and entering into his obedience? It is said to them: Among all those who sat back, whether we named them or omitted mentioning them, there is none who impugned his imamate or believed in its corruption. They only sat back from supporting him against the Muslims out of fear of that.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a historical-theological discussion about the Battle of the Camel, the differing views among Muslims regarding the actions of the Companions involved, and the explanation of the true cause of the battle. Baqillani begins by stating that the legal punishment (had) is only removed by the specific events he previously mentioned, and then addresses the issue of the fighting between Ali and his opponents (Talhah, al-Zubayr, and Aisha). He presents four main views among the Muslims: (1) Some consider this a matter of ijtihad, where each mujtahid is correct, as in other legal matters. (2) Some hold that the truth lies with Ali alone, and his opponents are mistaken but not sinful. (3) Some affirm that Ali was correct and his opponents were wrong, but they are forgiven. (4) Some claim that they repented, citing evidence such as al-Zubayr's return, Aisha's regret and weeping, and Talhah's dying act of pledging allegiance to Ali. Baqillani then mentions that the relied-upon evidence for this is the Prophet's hadith that ten Quraysh are in Paradise, included Talhah and al-Zubayr, implying they repented. He also notes that some Mu'tazila imams (like Amr ibn Ubayd and Wasil ibn Ata) suspend judgment, not knowing who was correct. Then Baqillani presents the view he considers correct and well-known: the battle was not premeditated but happened suddenly due to a conspiracy by the killers of Uthman. They had made peace, but the conspirators feared capture, so they started a war at dawn, shouting accusations of betrayal from both sides, causing each party to think the other had betrayed them. Thus, each side was defending itself. Baqillani argues that this interpretation makes both parties correct in their actions and obedient to Allah. Finally, he addresses an objection: if Ali's imamate was valid, why did some Companions (like Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, etc.) not support him? He answers that they did not deny his imamate but refrained from fighting out of fear of civil strife.

Key Terms
اجتهاد
إمامة
وقعة الجمل
توبة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Companions who fought Ali were sinful or disbelievers.
Correction: Baqillani shows they acted out of ijtihad and were not sinful; many repented or were forgiven.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, which view does he consider the correct and well-known one?
A) Both sides are correct through ijtihad.
B) The truth lies with Ali alone, and opponents are mistaken but not sinful.
C) The battle was a sudden conspiracy by the killers of Uthman.
D) The opponents repented from their actions.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani presents multiple valid interpretations of the Companions' actions in the Battle of the Camel, emphasizing that they acted out of ijtihad and were not sinful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Battle of the Camel, do you find yourself taking sides? Baqillani shows that even the Companions acted on ijtihad and were forgiven. How does this challenge your tendency to judge others in religious disagreements? What would it look like to assume good faith in a current dispute you are involved in?
?
Aisha wept and wished she had never been part of the battle. Think of a time you were involved in a conflict that you later regretted deeply. Did you seek forgiveness? This lesson reminds us that repentance and forgiveness are doors always open. Is there a relationship you need to mend today?
?
The killers of Uthman started the war through deceit. How often do outside forces exploit our divisions? Examine your own community: are there forces (media, rumors) that fuel division? What is your responsibility in not being a pawn in such games?

The Objection About Companions Not Supporting Ali
Baqillani answers an objection about Companions who did not support Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's response to the objection that some Companions did not support Ali, and how he defends them.

Core Idea
The Companions who did not support Ali did not deny his imamate; they refrained out of fear of civil strife.

After establishing the validity of Ali's imamate and the true cause of the battle, Baqillani addresses an important objection: if Ali was the rightful caliph, why did respected Companions like Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas not support him? This lesson examines Baqillani's concise and powerful response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the question posed: why did certain Companions not support Ali?
2
Study the answer
Baqillani's answer is that none of them impugned Ali's imamate; they only refrained out of fear of further conflict.
3
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how Baqillani upholds the integrity of all Companions while defending Ali's rightful position.

مذاهب المسلمين في إقامة الحد؛ إنما ينخلع بالأحداث التي ذكرناها من قبل فقط. فأما حربهما له على ذلك فإنه اجتهاد منهما وما أداهما الرأي إليه وهما من أهل الفقه والرأي؛ وكذلك عائشة. فمن الناس من يجعل هذه المسألة من مسائل الاجتهاد ويقول: إن كل مجتهد مصيب كإصابتهم في سائر مسائل الأحكام. ومنهم من يقول إن الحق منها في واحد، وهو رأي علي وقوله وإن مخالفه مخطىء في الاجتهاد خطأ لا يبلغ به الإثم والفسوق بل الإثم عنه موضوع. ومنهم من يقطع بصواب أمير المؤمنين وخطأ من خالفه ونازعه وأنه مغفور له. ومنهم من يقول: إنهم تابوا من ذلك ويستدل برجوع الزبير وندم عائشة إذا ذكروا لها يوم الجمل وبكائها حتى تبل خمارها وقولها: وددت أن لو كان لي عشرون ولداً من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كلهم مثل عبد الرحمن بن الحارث بن هشام، وأني تكلتهم، ولم يكن ما كان مني يوم الجمل، وقولها: لقد أحدقت بي يوم الجمل الأسنّة حتى صرت على البعير مثل اللجة. وأن طلحة قال لشاب من عسكر علي، وهو يجود بنفسه: أمدد يدك أبايعك لأمير المؤمنين، وما هذا نحوه. والمعتمد عندهم في ذلك قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: عشرة من قريش في الجنة وعد فيهم طلحة والزبير. قالوا: ولم يكن ليخبر بذلك إلا علم منه بأنهما سيتوبان مما أحدثاه ويوافيان بالندم والإقلاع. ومن أئمة المعتزلة من يقف في علي وطلحة والزبير وعائشة ولا يدري من المصيب منهم ومن المخطىء كعمرو بن عبيد وواصل بن عطاء من مال إلى قولهم. وقال جلّة من أهل العلم إن الوقعة بالبصرة بينهم كانت على غير عزيمة على الحرب بل فجاءة وكان على سبيل دفع كل واحد من الفريقين عن أنفسهم لظنه أن الفريق الآخر قد غدر بها لأن الأمر قد كان انتظم بينهم وتم الصلح والتفرق على الرضا فخاف قتلة عثمان من التمكن منهم والإحاطة بهم فاجتمعوا وتشاوروا واختلفوا ثم اتفقت آراؤهم على أن يفترقوا فرقتين ويبدؤوا بالحرب سحرة في العسكرين ويختلطوا ويصيح الفريق الذي في عسكر علي: غدر طلحة والزبير ويصيح الفريق الآخر الذي في عسكر طلحة والزبير: غدر علي! فتم لهم ذلك على ما دبروه ونشبت الحرب؛ فكان كل فريق منهم دافعا لمكروه عن نفسه ومانعاً من الإشاطة بدمه. وهذا صواب من الفريقين وطاعة الله تعالى، إذا وقع القتال والامتناع منهم على هذه السبيل. فهذا هو الصحيح المشهور وإليه نميل وبه نقول. فإن قال قائل: فإذا كانت إمامة علي من الصحة والثبوت بحيث وصفتم فما تقولون في تأخر سعد بن أبي وقاص وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن نفيل بن عمر ومحمد بن مسلمة وأسامة بن زيد وسلامة بن وقش وغير هؤلاء ممن يكثر عددهم وقعودهم عن نصرته والدخول في طاعته؟ قيل لهم: ليس في جميع القاعدين ممن أسميناه أو أضربنا عن ذكره من طعن في إمامته واعتقد فسادها وإنما قعدوا عن نصرته على حرب المسلمين لتخوفهم من ذلك.
The positions of Muslims regarding the establishment of the limit: it is only removed by the events we mentioned before. As for their fighting him for that, it was their ijtihad and what their opinion led them to, and they are people of jurisprudence and opinion; and likewise Aisha. Among the people, some make this issue one of ijtihad and say: every mujtahid is correct, like their correctness in all other legal issues. And among them are those who say that the truth lies in one of them, and it is the opinion and statement of Ali, and that whoever opposes him is mistaken in ijtihad, a mistake that does not reach the level of sin and disobedience, rather sin is waived from him. And among them are those who decide the correctness of the Commander of the Faithful and the error of those who opposed and contested him, and that it is forgiven for him. And among them are those who say that they repented from that, and they adduce the return of al-Zubayr and the regret of Aisha when they reminded her of the Day of the Camel and her weeping until her veil became wet, and her saying: 'I wish I had twenty sons from the Messenger of Allah, all of them like Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Harith ibn Hisham, and that I had lost them, and that what happened to me on the Day of the Camel had not happened,' and her saying: 'The spears surrounded me on the Day of the Camel until I became on the camel like a wave.' And that Talhah said to a youth in Ali's army, while he was dying: 'Extend your hand so that I pledge allegiance to you for the Commander of the Faithful,' and similar things. And the relied-upon among them regarding that is the saying of the Prophet: 'Ten from Quraysh are in Paradise,' including Talhah and al-Zubayr. They said: He would not have informed of that except out of knowledge that they would repent from what they had done and come with regret and desistance. And among the imams of the Mu'tazila are those who pause regarding Ali, Talhah, al-Zubayr, and Aisha, and do not know who is correct among them and who is mistaken, like Amr ibn Ubayd and Wasil ibn Ata who inclined to their statement. The Battle of the Camel: An Unintended Defensive Conflict
Baqillani describes the Battle of the Camel as an unintended defensive fight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's justification for the Battle of the Camel as an unintended defensive fight, and how the conspiracy of the Uthman murderers led to the conflict.

Core Idea
The Battle of the Camel was a tragic accident, sparked by a conspiracy to frame both sides.

This lesson explores Baqillani's explanation of one of the most controversial events in early Islamic history. He presents a defense of both Ali and his opponents, Talha and Zubayr, arguing that the battle was not a premeditated rebellion but a sudden, defensive reaction triggered by a conspiracy. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Context
Read the passage to grasp the background of the Battle of the Camel and the peace agreement that was in place before the conflict.
Notice that Baqillani emphasizes the prior peace and satisfaction of both parties.
2
Analyze the Conspiracy
Identify how the murderers of Uthman, fearing exposure, plotted to start the war by spreading false slogans in both camps.
This is the key turning point in Baqillani's narrative.
3
Evaluate the Defense
Consider Baqillani's conclusion that both parties were acting in self-defense and obedience to God, not as aggressors.
Reflect on why this interpretation matters for Sunni orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال جلّة من أهل العلم إن الوقعة بالبصرة بينهم كانت على غير عزيمة على الحرب بل فجاءة وكان على سبيل دفع كل واحد من الفريقين عن أنفسهم لظنه أن الفريق الآخر قد غدر بها لأن الأمر قد كان انتظم بينهم وتم الصلح والتفرق على الرضا فخاف قتلة عثمان من التمكن منهم والإحاطة بهم فاجتمعوا وتشاوروا واختلفوا ثم اتفقت آراؤهم على أن يفترقوا فرقتين ويبدؤوا بالحرب سُحْرَةً في العسكرين ويختلطوا ويصيح الفريق الذي في عسكر علي : غدر طلحة والزبير ويصيح الفريق الآخر الذي في عسكر طلحة والزبير غدر عليّ ! فتم لهم ذلك على ما دبروه ونَشِبَتْ الحرب؛ فكان كل فريق منهم لمكروه عن نفسه ومانعاً من الإشاطة بدمه. وهذا صواب من الفريقين دافعا وطاعة الله تعالى، إذا وقع القتال والامتناع منهم على هذه السبيل. فهذا هو الصحيح المشهور وإليه نميل وبه نقول .
And a group of the people of knowledge said that the incident at Basra between them was not based on a resolution for war, but rather suddenly, and it was in the way of each of the two parties defending themselves, because each thought that the other party had betrayed them, since the matter had been settled between them, peace had been concluded, and they had separated with satisfaction. Then the murderers of Uthman feared being seized and surrounded, so they gathered and consulted and disagreed, then their opinions agreed that they should split into two groups and start the war at dawn in the two camps, and mix, and the group in Ali's camp shout: 'Talha and Zubayr have betrayed!' and the other group in Talha and Zubayr's camp shout: 'Ali has betrayed!' So they accomplished that as they had planned, and war broke out. So each party was repelling harm from themselves and preventing the shedding of their blood. And this is correct from both parties as defenders and in obedience to Allah Almighty, if the fighting and resistance occurred in this manner. So this is the correct and well-known view, and to it we incline and by it we speak.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a historical-theological justification of the Battle of the Camel. Baqillani first reports the view of a group of scholars that the battle was not premeditated but a sudden outbreak. Each party was acting in self-defense, believing the other had betrayed the prior peace agreement. He then narrates how the murderers of Uthman, fearing exposure, conspired to start a conflict by spreading false slogans in both camps, which led to war. Each group was thus defending itself, not initiating aggression. Baqillani concludes that this is the correct and well-known view, and that both sides are excused as defenders, acting in obedience to God under the circumstances.

دفع
غدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Battle of the Camel was a premeditated rebellion against Ali's caliphate.
Correction: Baqillani argues it was a sudden defensive fight caused by a conspiracy of the murderers of Uthman.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what was the primary reason for the outbreak of the Battle of the Camel?
A) A premeditated rebellion against Ali's caliphate
B) A sudden defensive reaction based on mutual suspicion
C) An offensive war declared by Talha and Zubayr
D) A punishment for the murderers of Uthman

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends both parties in the Battle of the Camel as acting defensively, shifting blame to the conspirators who murdered Uthman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Baqillani says each side was acting in obedience to Allah while defending themselves. Is your instinct to defend yourself always justified? How can you distinguish between righteous defense and a reaction based on ego or misinformation?

Why Did Some Companions Not Fight for Ali?
Baqillani answers an objection about companions who did not support Ali militarily.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the reluctance of some companions to fight alongside Ali does not undermine their belief in his rightful imamate.

Core Idea
Abstaining from civil war does not mean denying the imam's authority.

This passage addresses a historical objection: if Ali was the rightful caliph, why did prominent companions like Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas refuse to support him militarily? Baqillani responds by showing that their abstention was not a rejection of his imamate but a precaution against the sin of killing fellow Muslims. He provides examples of their statements to clarify that they acknowledged Ali's authority and only feared the consequences of civil strife.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. First, understand the objector's question, then Baqillani's initial claim that none of those who sat back denied Ali's imamate.
Notice that Baqillani immediately clarifies their motive: fear of sin.
2
Examine the three examples
Study the statements attributed to three companions. For each, identify the reason given for not fighting and note that none of them say Ali is not the rightful imam.
The examples illustrate that their objection was to the action, not the person.
3
Understand the conclusion
Reflect on Baqillani's final sentence: 'And this is not a discredit to the imamate in any way.' Consider how this argument defends the integrity of the companions while upholding Ali's imamate.

فإن قال قائل : فإذا كانت إمامة عليّ من الصحة والثبوت بحيث وصفتم فما تقولون في تأخر سعد بن أبي وقاص وسعيد بن زيد بن عمرو بن د بن نفيل بن عمر ومحمد بن مسلمة وأسامة بن زيد وسلامة بن وَقش وغير الله وعبد هؤلاء ممن يكثر عددهم وقعودهم عن نصرته والدخول في طاعته؟ قيل لهم : ليس في جميع القاعدين ممن أسميناه أو أضربنا عن ذكره من طعن في إمامته واعتقد فسادها وإنما قعدوا عن نصرته على حرب المسلمين لتخوفهم من ذلك وتجنب الإثم فيه وظنهم موافقة العصيان في طاعته في هذا الفعل فلذلك احتجوا عليه في القعود ورووا له فيه الأخبار وقال منهم قائل: «لا أقاتل حتى تأتيني بسيف له لسان يعرف المؤمن من الكافر ويقول : هذا مؤمن وهذا كافر فاقتله! ولم يقل : إنك لست بإمام واجب الطاعة. وقال له محمد بعد مراجعته ومعارضته : إن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عهد إلي إذا وقعت فتنة بين المسلمين أن أكسر سيفي واتخذ مكانه سيفاً من خشب»(۱) وفي خبر آخر: «أن أغمد سيفي وأمْتَسِك في بيتي حتى تأتيني ميتة ماضية أو يد خاطئة (۲) ، فاحذر يا علي ! لا تكن أنت تلك اليد الخاطئة! ولم يقل له : لست بإمام مفروض الطاعة. وكذلك قال له أسامة بن زيد : قد علمت يا علي أنك لو دخلت بطن أسد لدخلتُ معك فيه ولكن لا مواساة في النار (۳) ولم يقل : إنك لست بإمام وإنما خاف من قتل المسلمين. وليس هذا من القدح في الإمامة بسبيل .
If someone says: 'If the imamate of Ali was as correct and established as you have described, what do you say about the delay of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and Sa'id ibn Zayd ibn Amr ibn [؟] ibn Nufayl, and Muhammad ibn Maslamah, and Usamah ibn Zayd, and Salamah ibn Waqsh, and others [؟] and [؟] of those whose number is great, and their sitting back from supporting him and entering into his obedience?' It is said to them: 'Among all those who sat back, whether we named them or omitted mention, there is not one who impugned his imamate or believed in its invalidity. Rather, they sat back from supporting him in fighting Muslims out of fear of that and to avoid sin in it, and their assumption that obedience to him in this action would be disobedience. That is why they argued with him about sitting back and narrated reports to him about it. One of them said: "I will not fight until you bring me a sword that has a tongue, which knows the believer from the disbeliever and says: This is a believer, this is a disbeliever, so kill him!" And he did not say: "You are not an imam whose obedience is obligatory." And Muhammad said to him after reviewing and opposing: "The Messenger of Allah ﷺ charged me that when a fitnah occurs among Muslims, I should break my sword and take in its place a sword of wood." And in another report: "That I sheathe my sword and hold back in my house until a certain death or a mistaken hand comes to me. Beware, O Ali, lest you be that mistaken hand!" And he did not say to him: "You are not an imam whose obedience is obligatory." Similarly, Usamah ibn Zayd said to him: "I know, O Ali, that if you entered the belly of a lion, I would enter with you, but there is no sympathy in the Fire." And he did not say: "You are not an imam." He only feared killing Muslims. And this is not a discredit to the imamate in any way.'
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer format. The objector asks: If Ali's imamate was valid, why did certain prominent companions (like Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, etc.) refrain from supporting him militarily? Baqillani responds by affirming that none of those who sat back denied Ali's imamate or believed it invalid. Their reason was fear of participating in civil war among Muslims and avoiding sin. They suspected that obedience to Ali in this particular matter might involve disobedience to God. To support their position, they cited reports from the Prophet. Baqillani gives three examples of their statements: (1) One companion demanded a supernatural sword to distinguish believers from disbelievers. (2) Muhammad ibn Maslamah recalled the Prophet's instruction to break his sword in times of fitnah and not to fight. (3) Usamah ibn Zayd expressed willingness to follow Ali into any danger except the Fire, meaning he feared that fighting would lead to sin. In all these cases, none said Ali was not the rightful imam. Therefore, their abstention does not constitute a discredit to the imamate.

إمامة
قعود
فتنة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Companions who did not fight alongside Ali rejected his imamate.
Correction: Baqillani shows they acknowledged his imamate but feared sin in civil war.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why did companions like Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas refrain from supporting Ali in battle?
A) They denied Ali's imamate
B) They feared sinning by participating in a civil war among Muslims
C) They were waiting for a divine sign
D) They were forced by the Umayyads

Key Takeaway
The companions' abstention from supporting Ali militarily was based on fear of fitnah and sin, not on a denial of his rightful imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow believer making a decision that seems to go against what you think is right, do you immediately assume they have rejected the truth? The companions did not accuse Ali of being wrong—they simply acted differently based on their own fear of God. Can you withhold judgment and assume good faith in those who disagree with you, especially in matters of great ambiguity?
?
The companions refused to fight even though they acknowledged Ali's imamate because they feared killing other Muslims. Have you ever avoided a religious duty because you thought it might lead to sin? Was that fear genuine, or was it an excuse to avoid difficulty?
?
One companion said, 'There is no sympathy in the Fire.' He refused to enter Paradise with Ali if it meant killing believers. Is your love for the truth and loyalty to a leader strong enough to resist sinful actions even when that leader commands them? How do you handle the conflict between obedience to authority and obedience to your conscience?

Ali's Inability to Punish Uthman's Killers
Baqillani enumerates obstacles to Ali's retribution for Uthman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practical and legal reasons why Ali could not exact retribution for Uthman's murder.

Core Idea
Ali faced legal and practical obstacles, not weakness, in punishing Uthman's killers.

Baqillani addresses a common historical and sectarian question: why didn't Ali punish those who killed Uthman? The answer lies not in Ali's weakness but in the complex legal and practical realities he faced. This passage lays out the obstacles that prevented him from establishing retribution.

Guided Path
1

The passage is incomplete; it ends mid-sentence. Focus on the obstacles given.
2

Baqillani lists several reasons Ali could not punish the killers. Find each one: unknown identities, lack of evidence, no confession, and the role of Ali's own supporters.
Each obstacle is a distinct legal or practical barrier.
3
Reflect on the role of Ali's supporters
Note that some of Ali's companions (e.g., al-Ashtar, Ibn Saba') were critical of Uthman. How did their stance affect Ali's ability to act?
This adds a political dimension to the legal obstacles.
